===== [#50634753_pgfId-1002532]##Array

[#50634753_pgfId-1003610]##An XML array is mapped to a Java array with
the operator _[]_ . The JAX-RPC specification requires support for the
following types of XML array definitions:

[#50634753_pgfId-1075466]##An array derived from the _soapenc:Array_ by
restriction using the _wsdl:arrayType_ attribute. This case is specified
in the WSDL 1.1 link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_91453[See Web Services
Description Language (WSDL) 1.1: http://www.w3.org/TR/wsdl]
specification

{empty}[#50634753_pgfId-1075471]##An array derived from _soapenc:Array_
by restriction as specified in the SOAP 1.1 specification
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_73033[See W3C Note: SOAP 1.1:
http://www.w3.org/TR/SOAP/]

[#50634753_pgfId-1064184]##The type of Java array element is determined
based on the schema for the XML array. Note that the array dimension is
omitted in the declaration of a Java array. The number of elements in a
Java array is determined at the creation time rather than when an array
is declared.

[#50634753_pgfId-1067363]##The standard type mapping supports XML arrays
with multiple dimensions.

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1002992]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1075435]##The following shows an example of an array
derived from the _soapenc:Array_ by restriction using the
_wsdl:arrayType_ attribute. This array maps to the Java _int[]_ :

[#50634753_pgfId-1075436]##<complexType name="ArrayOfInt">

[#50634753_pgfId-1075437]## <complexContent>

[#50634753_pgfId-1075438]## <restriction base="soapenc:Array">

[#50634753_pgfId-1075439]## <attribute ref="soapenc:arrayType"

[#50634753_pgfId-1075489]## wsdl:arrayType="xsd:int[]"/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1075440]## </restriction>

[#50634753_pgfId-1075441]## </complexContent>

[#50634753_pgfId-1075442]##</complexType>

[#50634753_pgfId-1075363]##The following example shows an XML array
formed by the restriction of the _soapenc:Array_ _._

[#50634753_pgfId-1075364]##<!-- Schema fragment -->

[#50634753_pgfId-1075365]##<complexType name=”ArrayOfPhoneNumbers”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1075366]## <complexContent>

[#50634753_pgfId-1075367]## <restriction base=”soapenc:Array”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1075368]## <sequence>

[#50634753_pgfId-1075369]## <element name=”phoneNumber”

[#50634753_pgfId-1075370]## type=”xsd:string” maxOccurs=”unbounded”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1075371]## </sequence>

[#50634753_pgfId-1075372]## </restriction>

[#50634753_pgfId-1075373]## </complexContent>

[#50634753_pgfId-1075374]##</complexType>

[#50634753_pgfId-1075375]##The above XML array maps to a _String[]_ in
the Java mapping. In this example, _java.lang.String_ (mapping of the
base element type _xsd:string_ in the above XML array) is used as the
element type in the mapped Java array.

[#50634753_pgfId-1017999]##The following example shows a schema fragment
and instance for a polymorphic array.

[#50634753_pgfId-1018000]##<!-- Schema fragment -->

[#50634753_pgfId-1018001]##<element name=”myNumbers”
type=”soapenc:Array”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1018002]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1042103]##<!-- Schema instance -->

[#50634753_pgfId-1018003]##<myNumbers soapenc:arrayType=”xsd:int[2]”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1018004]## <number>1</number>

[#50634753_pgfId-1018005]## <number>2</number>

[#50634753_pgfId-1018006]##</myNumbers>

[#50634753_pgfId-1018007]##The above XML array maps to a Java array of
_java.lang.Object_ . The operator _[]_ is applied to the mapped Java
array. Note that above XML array is not mapped to a Java array of
integers, since the type ( _xsd:int_ ) of array members is determined by
the inspection of the _soapenc:arrayType_ attribute in the schema
instance.

[#50634753_pgfId-1003663]##An array can also contain struct values. The
following schema fragment shows an example:

[#50634753_pgfId-1003691]##<!-- XML schema fragment -->

[#50634753_pgfId-1003692]##<complexType name=”Book”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1046432]## <all>

[#50634753_pgfId-1003693]## <element name=”author” type=”xsd:string”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1003694]## <element name=”preface” type=”xsd:string”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1003695]## <element name=”price” type=”xsd:float”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1046433]## </all>

[#50634753_pgfId-1003696]##</complexType>

[#50634753_pgfId-1003701]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1003667]##<complexType name=”ArrayOfBooks”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1046434]##<complexContent>

[#50634753_pgfId-1046435]## <restriction base=”soapenc:Array”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1046442]## <sequence>

[#50634753_pgfId-1003668]## <element name=”book” type=”tns:Book”
maxOccurs=”unbounded”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1046443]## <sequence>

[#50634753_pgfId-1046444]## </restriction>

[#50634753_pgfId-1046445]##</complexContext>

[#50634753_pgfId-1003670]##</complexType>

[#50634753_pgfId-1003707]##The above XML array maps to _Book[]_ in the
Java mapping. Refer to the Java mapping of an XML struct for details on
how _Book_ type has been mapped.

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1064198]##[#50634753_39235]##[#50634753_76085]##XML Struct and Complex Type

[#50634753_pgfId-1067387]##The JAX-RPC specification supports the
mapping of the following types of XML struct:

{empty}[#50634753_pgfId-1067388]##The _xsd:complexType_ with both
sequence of elements of either simple or complex type. Refer to the
_xsd:sequence_ link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_26228[See W3C Recommendation
“XML Schema Part 2: Datatypes”: http://www.w3.org/TR/xmlschema-2/]

[#50634753_pgfId-1064217]##The _xsd:complexType_ with _xsd:all_
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_26228[See W3C Recommendation “XML Schema Part
2: Datatypes”: http://www.w3.org/TR/xmlschema-2/] based unordered
grouping of elements of either simple or complex type

[#50634753_pgfId-1109804]##The _xsd:complexType_ with
_xsd:simpleContent_ used to declare a complex type by extension of an
existing simple type

[#50634753_pgfId-1097052]##In all cases, attribute uses specified using
either the _xsd:attribute_ or _xsd:attributeGroup_ elements are
supported.

[#50634753_pgfId-1109803]##An XML struct maps to a JavaBeans class with
the same name as the type of the XML struct. If the struct is anonymous,
then the name of the nearest enclosing _xsd:element_ , _xsd:complexType_
or _xsd:simpleType_ is used instead.

[#50634753_pgfId-1110295]##The mapped JavaBeans class provides a pair of
getter and setter methods for each property mapped from the member
elements and attributes of the XML struct.

[#50634753_pgfId-1067404]##The identifier and Java type of a property in
the JavaBeans class is mapped from the _name_ and _type_ of the
corresponding member element (or attribute) in the XML struct. Refer to
the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_96144[See XML Names] for the mapping of XML
names to Java identifiers.

[#50634753_pgfId-1109493]##Note that, according to JavaBeans
conventions, the getter method for a boolean property uses the prefix
“is” instead of “get”, e.g. _isRequired()_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1109810]##For complex types defined using
_xsd:simpleContent_ and extending a simple type T, the corresponding
JavaBean class will contain an additional property named “ __value_ “
and whose type is mapped from the simple type T according to the rules
in this specification.

[#50634753_pgfId-1064348]##The instances of the mapped JavaBeans class
must be capable of marshaling to and from the corresponding XML struct
representation.

[#50634753_pgfId-1096905]##An element in a complex type with the
_maxOccurs_ attribute set to a non-negative integer greater than 1 or
_unbounded_ is mapped to a Java array with a pair of setter and getter
methods in the JavaBeans class. The Java type of the array is mapped
from the _type_ attribute of the XML element. Refer to the following
example.

[#50634753_pgfId-1098188]##The JAX-RPC specification does not require
support for all different combinations of the occurrence constraints (
_minOccurs_ , _maxOccurs_ ).

[#50634753_pgfId-1109878]##Additionally, the _xsd:any_ element can occur
within complex type declarations to represent element wildcards. In this
context, it will result in an additional property on the JavaBean
corresponding to the containing complex type. This property will be
called “ __any_ ” and will have _javax.xml.soap.SOAPElement_ as its
type, unless the _xml:any_ element has a _maxOccurs_ attribute with a
value greater than 1, in which case its type will be
_javax.xml.soap.SOAPElement[]_ .

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1096974]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1096975]##The following example shows a struct of the
type _Book_ and its schema fragment and instance:

[#50634753_pgfId-1096976]##<!-- XML Schema fragment -->

[#50634753_pgfId-1096978]##<complexType name=”Book”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1096979]## <sequence>

[#50634753_pgfId-1096980]## <element name=”authors” type=”xsd:string”
maxOccurs=”10”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1096981]## <element name=”preface” type=”xsd:string”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1096982]## <element name=”price” type=”xsd:float”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1096983]## </sequence>

[#50634753_pgfId-1096984]##</complexType>

[#50634753_pgfId-1096993]##The above XML struct is mapped to a JavaBeans
class as follows:

[#50634753_pgfId-1096994]##// Java

[#50634753_pgfId-1096995]##public class Book \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1096996]## // ...

[#50634753_pgfId-1096997]## public String[] getAuthors() \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1096998]## public void setAuthors(String[] authors) \{
... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1096999]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1097000]## public String getPreface() \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1097001]## public void setPreface(String preface) \{
... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1097002]## public float getPrice() \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1097003]## public void setPrice(float price) \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1096972]##}

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1109819]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1109820]##The following schema fragment shows a complex
type derived by extension from the xsd:string simple type:

[#50634753_pgfId-1109849]##<!-- XML Schema fragment -->

[#50634753_pgfId-1109822]##<complexType name=”CountedString”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1109823]## <simpleContent>

[#50634753_pgfId-1109850]## <extension base=”xsd:string>

[#50634753_pgfId-1109851]## <attribute name=”counter” type=”xsd:int”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1109852]## </extension>

[#50634753_pgfId-1109853]## </simpleContent>

[#50634753_pgfId-1109854]##</complexType>

[#50634753_pgfId-1109829]##The complex type above is mapped to the
following JavaBeans class:

[#50634753_pgfId-1109830]##// Java

[#50634753_pgfId-1109831]##public class CountedString \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1109832]## // ...

[#50634753_pgfId-1109833]## public String get_value() \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1109834]## public void set_value(String value) \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1109835]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1109836]## public int getCounter() \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1109837]## public void setCounter(int counter) \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1109838]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1109817]## 

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1096900]##[#50634753_58682]##Enumeration

[#50634753_pgfId-1003157]##An XML enumeration is a specific list of
distinct values appropriate for a base type. The XML Schema Part 2:
Datatypes specification supports enumerations for all simple built-in
types except for _xsd:boolean_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1003158]##An XML enumeration is mapped by default to a
Java class with the same name as the enumeration type. If the
enumeration is anonymous, then the name of the nearest enclosing
_xsd:attribute_ , _xsd:element_ , _xsd:simpleType_ or _xsd:complexType_
is used instead.

[#50634753_pgfId-1112329]##In order to be compatible with the JAXB 1.0
specification link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_99925[See JAXB specification:
http://java.sun.com/xml/jaxb/], in addition to the default mapping given
above JAX-RPC implementations are required to support mapping anonymous
enumerations using the rules for simple types derived via restriction
given in link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_43750[See Simple Types Derived By
Restriction].

[#50634753_pgfId-1111104]##The mapped Java class declares a _getValue_
method, two static data members per label, an integer conversion method
and a constructor as follows:

[#50634753_pgfId-1003173]##//Java

[#50634753_pgfId-1018097]##public class <enumeration_name> \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1003325]## // ...

[#50634753_pgfId-1094126]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1094125]## // Constructor

[#50634753_pgfId-1003326]## protected <enumeration_name>(<base_type>
value) \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1003174]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1003323]## // One for each label in the enumeration

[#50634753_pgfId-1003299]## public static final <base_type> _<label> =
<value>;

[#50634753_pgfId-1003179]## public static final <enumeration_name>
<label> =

[#50634753_pgfId-1003180]## new <enumeration_name>(_<label>);

[#50634753_pgfId-1003177]##

[#50634753_pgfId-1003182]## // Gets the value for a enumerated value

[#50634753_pgfId-1094130]## public <base_type> getValue() \{...}

[#50634753_pgfId-1003178]##

[#50634753_pgfId-1003181]## // Gets enumeration with a specific value

[#50634753_pgfId-1094078]## // Required to throw
java.lang.IllegalArgumentException if

[#50634753_pgfId-1094085]## // any invalid value is specified

[#50634753_pgfId-1094165]## public static <enumeration_name>
fromValue(<base_type> value) \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1094166]## ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1094171]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1094194]## // Gets enumeration from a String

[#50634753_pgfId-1094178]## // Required to throw
java.lang.IllegalArgumentException if

[#50634753_pgfId-1094179]## // any invalid value is specified

[#50634753_pgfId-1094172]## public static <enumeration_name>
fromString(String value)\{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1094167]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1094175]## // Returns String representation of the
enumerated value

[#50634753_pgfId-1094141]## public String toString() \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1094142]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1073643]## public boolean equals(Object obj) \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1073644]## public int hashCode() \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1003176]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1094088]##All _<label> and _<label>_ used in the mapped
Java class (for XML enumeration) are required to be valid Java
identifiers. According to the Java language specification, a Java
identifier cannot have the same spelling as a Java keyword, _Boolean_
literal or _null_ literal.

[#50634753_pgfId-1094112]##If one or more enumerated values in an XML
enumeration cannot map to valid Java identifiers (examples are “3.14”,
“int”), the mapped Java class is required to use Java identifiers
_value<1..N>_ and _ _value<1..N>_ for _<label>_ and __<label>_ (as in
the above mapping code snippet) respectively. The numeric suffix starts
from 1 and increments by 1 per value in the XML enumeration. Examples
are __value1_ , _value1_ , _value2_ and __value2_ .

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1003197]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1003198]##The following shows an example of XML
enumeration and its schema fragment:

[#50634753_pgfId-1018101]##<!-- XML Schema fragment -->

[#50634753_pgfId-1018109]##<element name=”EyeColor”
type=”EyeColorType”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1018102]##<simpleType name=”EyeColorType”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1046400]##<restriction base=”xsd:string”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1018103]## <enumeration value=”green”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1018104]## <enumeration value=”blue”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1018105]##</restriction>

[#50634753_pgfId-1046402]##</simpleType>

[#50634753_pgfId-1003236]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1018108]##<!-- XML Schema instance -->

[#50634753_pgfId-1060039]##<EyeColor>green</EyeColor>

[#50634753_pgfId-1003232]##The following code snippet show the Java
mapping for the above XML enumeration:

[#50634753_pgfId-1003209]##//Java

[#50634753_pgfId-1044127]##public class EyeColorType \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1003316]## // Constructor

[#50634753_pgfId-1003317]## protected EyeColorType(String value) \{ ...
}

[#50634753_pgfId-1003253]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1003320]## public static final String _green = “green”;

[#50634753_pgfId-1003256]## public static final String _blue = “blue”;

[#50634753_pgfId-1003254]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1003246]## public static final EyeColorType green = new
EyeColorType(_green);

[#50634753_pgfId-1003269]## public static final EyeColorType blue = new
EyeColorType(_blue);

[#50634753_pgfId-1003267]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1003307]## public String getValue() \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1067416]## public static EyeColorType fromValue(String
value) \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1073638]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1094193]## public boolean equals(Object obj) \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1073639]## public int hashCode() \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1003112]## // ... Other methods not shown

[#50634753_pgfId-1094192]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1112363]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1112366]##Here’s the same XML enumeration type, this
type defined as an anonymous type:

[#50634753_pgfId-1112349]##<!-- XML Schema fragment -->

[#50634753_pgfId-1112350]##<element name=”EyeColor”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1112351]## <simpleType>

[#50634753_pgfId-1112352]## <restriction base=”xsd:string”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1112353]## <enumeration value=”green”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1112354]## <enumeration value=”blue”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1112355]## </restriction>

[#50634753_pgfId-1112356]## </simpleType>

[#50634753_pgfId-1112379]##</element>

[#50634753_pgfId-1112357]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1109659]##The default mapping for this enumeration type
is the same as for the non-anonymous case. Additionally, implementations
are also required to support mapping this enumeration type to the
_java.lang.String_ type, so as to be compatible with the JAXB 1.0
specification.

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1109661]##[#50634753_43750]##Simple Types Derived By Restriction

[#50634753_pgfId-1109660]##The XML Schema specification allows the
definition of new simple types obtained by restricting an existing
simple type. Restrictions on the set of allowed values are specified
using one or more of 12 predefined facets.

[#50634753_pgfId-1109703]##A simple type derived by restriction from
another simple type, referred to as its base type, is mapped to the same
Java type that its base type is mapped to. If its base type does not
have a standard JAX-RPC mapping (i.e. is unsupported), then the derived
type itself is unsupported.

[#50634753_pgfId-1109705]##Several built-in types defined in the XML
Schema specification are derived by restriction from other types for
which JAX-RPC provides a standard mapping. Such types must in
consequence be mapped according to the rules in the preceding
paragraphs.

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1109717]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1109710]##The built-in _xsd:normalizedString_ type is
derived by restriction from _xsd:string_ , hence it must be mapped to
_java.lang.String_ .

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1109712]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1109713]##The following schema fragment defines a new
simple type by restriction of the _xsd:int_ type. Consequently, it must
be mapped to the Java _int_ type.

[#50634753_pgfId-1109685]##<!-- XML Schema fragment -->

[#50634753_pgfId-1109687]##<simpleType name=”OneToTenType”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1109688]## <restriction base=”xsd:int”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1109689]## <minInclusive value=”1”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1109690]## <maxInclusive value=”10”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1109691]## </restriction>

[#50634753_pgfId-1109692]##</simpleType>

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1109662]##[#50634753_26103]##Simple Types Derived Using xsd:list

[#50634753_pgfId-1109663]##In XML Schema, simple type definitions can
specify xsd:list as their derivation mechanism. In this case, they also
specify an _item type_ which must itself be a simple type.

[#50634753_pgfId-1109757]##Simple types defined using _xsd:list_ and
whose item type has a standard JAX-RPC mapping are mapped to
arrays.These types include all built-in XML Schema types defined in the
same way, such as _xsd:NMTOKENS_ . The component type of the resulting
array is mapped from the item type of the simpel type.

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1109762]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1111988]##The following schema fragment defines a new
simple type “list of QNames” which is mapped to the
_javax.xml.namespace.QName[]_ type.

[#50634753_pgfId-1111989]##<!-- XML Schema fragment -->

[#50634753_pgfId-1109765]##<simpleType name=”QNameList”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1109766]## <list itemType=”xsd:QName”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1109770]##</simpleType>

[#50634753_pgfId-1109759]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1109760]## 

==== [#50634753_pgfId-1109652]##

image:jaxrpc-5.gif[image]

WSDL to Java Mapping[#50634753_51248]##

[#50634753_pgfId-1109654]##This section specifies the mapping of a
service described in a WSDL document to the corresponding Java
representation.

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1020447]##WSDL [#50634753_33943]##Document

[#50634753_pgfId-1070940]##A WSDL document is mapped to a Java package.
The fully qualified name of the mapped Java package is specific to an
application and is specified during the WSDL to Java mapping. A WSDL to
Java mapping tool is required to support the configuration of the
application specific package name during the mapping.

[#50634753_pgfId-1070950]##Note that the JAX-RPC specification does not
specify the standard mapping of a namespace definition (in a WSDL
document) to the corresponding Java package name. However, the JAX-RPC
requires that a namespace definition in a WSDL document must be mapped
to a unique Java package name. The name of the mapped Java package must
follow the package naming conventions defined in the Java Language
Specification link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_94614[See Java Language
Specification: http://java.sun.com/docs/books/jls/].

[#50634753_pgfId-1044180]##The WSDL 1.1 specification allows references
to the various WSDL definitions (examples: _portType_ , _message_ ).
Such _QName_ based references in WSDL are mapped based on the Java
package and name scoping conventions.

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1005292]##Extensibility Elements

[#50634753_pgfId-1018228]##The WSDL 1.1 specification allows definition
of extensibility elements (that may be specific to a binding or
technology) under various element definitions.

[#50634753_pgfId-1018231]##The JAX-RPC specification specifies mapping
of the extensibility elements for SOAP and MIME bindings. Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_75805[See SOAP Binding] and
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_29571[See WSDL Requirements]. However, the
JAX-RPC specification does not address mapping of any vendor specific
extensibility elements. A JAX-RPC implementation may support mapping of
WSDL extensibility elements at the cost of interoperability and
application portability.

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1018224]##WSDL [#50634753_43187]##Port Type

[#50634753_pgfId-1018295]##A WSDL port type is a named set of abstract
operations and messages involved.

[#50634753_pgfId-1003724]##A WSDL port type is mapped to a Java
interface (termed a Service Endpoint Interface) that extends the
_java.rmi.Remote_ interface. The mapping of a _wsdl:portType_ to a
service endpoint interface may use the _wsdl:binding_ element. Refer to
the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_63057[See SOAP Binding in WSDL] for details
on the use of the _soap:binding_ definition in the mapping of a WSDL
port type.

[#50634753_pgfId-1107611]##The _name_ of the Service endpoint interface
is mapped from the _name_ attribute of the _wsdl:portType_ element. Note
that a port type name attribute defines a unique name among all the port
types defined in an enclosing WSDL document. Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_96144[See XML Names] for the mapping of the XML
names to Java identifiers.

[#50634753_pgfId-1107604]##The mapped Java service endpoint interface
contains methods mapped from the _wsdl:operation_ elements defined in
the _wsdl:portType_ . Refer to the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_88615[See
WSDL Operation] for the standard mapping of a _wsdl:operation_
definition.

[#50634753_pgfId-1003867]##Since WSDL does not support inheritance of
the port types, the standard Java mapping of the WSDL port type does not
define support for the inheritance of the mapped Java interfaces.

[#50634753_pgfId-1028795]##Each method of the mapped Java interface is
required to declare _java.rmi._ _RemoteException_ in its throws clause.
A _RemoteException_ is the common superclass for exceptions related to a
remote method invocation. Examples are: _java.rmi.MarshalException_ ,
_java.rmi.ConnectException_ . Refer to the J2SE
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_70636[See J2SE: http://java.sun.com/j2se/]
documentation for more details on the _RemoteException_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1028807]##A method may also throw service specific
exceptions based on the mapping of a WSDL faults. Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_91875[See WSDL Fault] for more details.

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1003766]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1003789]##The following is an example of a port type
definition in a WSDL document:

[#50634753_pgfId-1003790]## _<!-- WSDL Extract -->_

[#50634753_pgfId-1018261]## _<message name=”getLastTradePrice”>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1003802]## _<part name=”tickerSymbol”
type=”xsd:string”/>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1003804]## _</message>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1003811]## _<message name=”getLastTradePriceResponse”>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1003812]## _<part name=”result” type=”xsd:float”/>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1003813]## _</message>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1003809]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1003801]## _<portType name=”StockQuoteProvider”>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1003792]## _<operation name=”getLastTradePrice”_

[#50634753_pgfId-1003799]## _parameterOrder=”tickerSymbol”>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1003793]## _<input message=”tns:getLastTradePrice”/>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1003794]## _<output
message=”tns:getLastTradePriceResponse”/>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1003795]## _</operation>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1003796]## _</portType>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1003798]##The above WSDL port type definition maps to
the following Java service endpoint interface:

[#50634753_pgfId-1003827]##//Java

[#50634753_pgfId-1018274]##public interface StockQuoteProvider extends
java.rmi.Remote \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1003828]## float getLastTradePrice(String tickerSymbol)

[#50634753_pgfId-1003833]## throws java.rmi.RemoteException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1003829]##}

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1004193]##WSDL [#50634753_88615]##Operation

[#50634753_pgfId-1073659]##A _wsdl:operation_ defined in a
_wsdl:portType_ maps to a Java method on the mapped Java service
endpoint interface. The mapping of a _wsdl:operation_ to a Java method
may include the use of the _wsdl:binding_ element. Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_63057[See SOAP Binding in WSDL] for the use of
the _soap:binding_ element in the mapping of a WSDL operation.

[#50634753_pgfId-1073660]##A _wsdl:operation_ is named by the _name_
attribute. The operation _name_ maps to the name of the corresponding
method on the mapped Java service endpoint interface. Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_96144[See XML Names] for the mapping of XML
names to Java identifiers.

[#50634753_pgfId-1005407]##Note that the WSDL 1.1 specification does not
require that operation names be unique. To support overloading of
operations, the _wsdl:binding_ element identifies correct operation by
providing the _name_ attributes of the corresponding _wsdl:input_ and
_wsdl:output_ elements. Refer to the WSDL 1.1 for complete details.

[#50634753_pgfId-1097521]##In the WSDL to Java mapping, overloaded
operations are mapped to overloaded Java methods provided the
overloading does not cause any conflicts in the mapped Java interface
declaration and follows the Java Language specification
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_94614[See Java Language Specification:
http://java.sun.com/docs/books/jls/].

[#50634753_pgfId-1018313]##The JAX-RPC specification supports the
mapping of operations with _request_ - _response_ and _one-way_
transmission primitives. The standard Java mapping of operations defined
with other transmission primitives ( _notification_ , _solicit-response_
) is considered out of scope in the JAX-RPC specification.

[#50634753_pgfId-1005412]##The message parts in the _wsdl:input_ and
_wsdl:output_ elements defined in an abstract WSDL operation are mapped
to parameters on the corresponding Java method signature. The name of
the Java method parameter is mapped from the _name_ attribute of the
corresponding message _part_ . The optional _wsdl:fault_ element maps to
an exception. Refer to the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_91875[See WSDL
Fault] for more details on the Java mapping of WSDL faults.

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1005404]##Parameter Passing Modes

[#50634753_pgfId-1018360]##The JAX-RPC specification does not support a
pass by reference mode for a remote service. JAX-RPC does not support
passing of a _java.rmi.Remote_ instance in a remote method invocation.

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1044250]##WSDL parameterOrder

[#50634753_pgfId-1091607]##According to the WSDL 1.1 specification, a
request-response operation may specify a list of parameters using the
_parameterOrder_ attribute. The value of the _parameterOrder_ attribute
follows these rules:

[#50634753_pgfId-1091608]##The _parameterOrder_ attribute reflects the
order of the parameters in the RPC signature

[#50634753_pgfId-1091609]##The return value part is not present in the
_parameterOrder_ list

[#50634753_pgfId-1091610]##If a part name appears in both the input and
output message with the same type, it is an _inout_ parameter

[#50634753_pgfId-1091611]##If a part name appears in only the
_wsdl:input_ message, it is an _in_ parameter

[#50634753_pgfId-1091612]##If a part name appears in only the
_wsdl:output_ message, it is an _out_ parameter

[#50634753_pgfId-1094335]##The order of parameters in an RPC signature
follows these rules:

[#50634753_pgfId-1094336]##Part names are either listed in the
_parameterOrder_ attribute or are unlisted. If there is no
_parameterOrder_ attribute, then all part names are considered unlisted.

[#50634753_pgfId-1094383]##If the _parameterOrder_ attribute is
specified, then all part names from the input message must be listed.
The part names from the output message may or may not be listed.

[#50634753_pgfId-1094394]##Listed part names appear first in the method
signature in the order that they are listed in the _parameterOrder_
attribute.

[#50634753_pgfId-1094401]##Unlisted part names appear following the
listed part names in the order in which these parts appear in the
message: first, the input message’s part names; next, the output
message’s part names. If an unlisted part is a component of an _inout_
parameter, then it appears in the order in which its corresponding part
appears in the input message (the order of output message parts is
ignored for _inout_ parameters).

[#50634753_pgfId-1094351]##If there is a single unlisted output part
that is not a component of an inout parameter, then it is the return
type. Otherwise, the return type is _void_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1094283]##The JAX-RPC specification specifies the
following rules for the _in_ , _out_ and _inout_ parameter passing modes
and return value:

[#50634753_pgfId-1091614]##An _in_ parameter is passed as copy. The
value of the _in_ parameter is copied before a remote method invocation.

[#50634753_pgfId-1091618]##The return value is created as a copy and
returned to the caller from a remote method invocation. The caller
becomes the owner of the returned object after completion of the remote
method invocation.

[#50634753_pgfId-1091619]##The _out_ and _inout_ parameters are passed
by copy. Parameter passing mode for _out_ and _inout_ parameters uses
_Holder_ classes. Refer to the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_94013[See Holder
Classes]. A service client provides an instance of a _Holder_ class that
is passed by value for either _out_ or _inout_ parameter. The contents
of the _Holder_ class are modified in the remote method invocation and
the service client uses the changed contents after the method invocation
returns.

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1018753]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1018754]##The following is an example of a port type
definition in a WSDL document:

[#50634753_pgfId-1018755]##<!-- WSDL Example -->

[#50634753_pgfId-1018786]##<message name=”StockQuoteInput”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1018756]## <part name=”tickerSymbol”
type=”xsd:string”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1018757]##</message>

[#50634753_pgfId-1018758]##<message name=”StockQuoteOutput”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1018759]## <part name=”lastTradePrice”
type=”xsd:float”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1018760]## <part name=”volume” type=”xsd:int”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1018761]## <part name=”bid” type=”xsd:float”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1018764]##

ask”>

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1003932]##[#50634753_94013]##Holder Classes

[#50634753_pgfId-1018541]##The JAX-RPC specification requires use of the
_Holder_ classes as part of the standard Java mapping of a WSDL
operation. The use of _Holder_ classes enables the mapping to preserve
the intended _wsdl:operation_ signature and parameter passing semantics.

[#50634753_pgfId-1018542]##The JAX-RPC specification includes _Holder_
classes for the Java mapping of the simple XML data types (including
_xsd:base64Binary_ , _xsd.hexBinary_ , _soapenc:base64_ ) in the j
_avax.xml.rpc.holders_ package. Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_93728[See Simple Types] for the Java mapping of
the simple XML data types.

[#50634753_pgfId-1097068]##The _Holder_ classes for the Java primitive
types are defined in the _javax.xml. rpc.holders_ package. The name of
the _Holder_ class is the name of the Java primitive type appended with
the suffix _Holder_ . The initial letter of the Java type name is
capitalized. An example is _javax.xml.rpc.holders.FloatHolder_ for the
Java primitive type _float_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1097057]##The name of the _Holder_ class for a Java
wrapper class (that wraps a primitive Java type) is derived by appending
the suffix _WrapperHolder_ to the name of the wrapper class. These
holders for the Java wrapper classes are also packaged in the
_javax.xml.rpc. holders_ package. An example is the
_javax.xml.rpc.holders.FloatWrapperHolder_ class for the wrapper class
_java.lang.Float_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1044371]##A WSDL to Java mapping tool generates
_Holder_ classes for XML data types other than the simple XML data
types. Examples are _Holder_ classes generated for the complex XML types
and extended simple XML data types based on the XML schema
specification.

[#50634753_pgfId-1003940]##For the complex XML data types, the name of
the _Holder_ class is constructed by appending _Holder_ to the name of
the corresponding Java class. These generated _Holder_ classes are
packaged as part of the generated sub package named _holders_ in the
WSDL to Java mapping. Refer to the section
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_33943[See WSDL Document] for the mapping of the
Java package. An example is _com.example.holders.BookHolder_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1097092]##The name of the _Holder_ class in the Java
mapping of an XML array is the name of the complex type (first letter
capitalized) appended with the _Holder_ suffix. Refer to the example
later in this section.

[#50634753_pgfId-1003941]##Each _Holder_ class provides the following
methods and fields:

[#50634753_pgfId-1003950]##A public field named _value_ . The type of
_value_ is the mapped Java type

{empty}[#50634753_pgfId-1003942]##A default constructor that initializes
the _value_ field to a default value. The default values for the Java
types are as specified in the Java Language Specification
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_94614[See Java Language Specification:
http://java.sun.com/docs/books/jls/]

[#50634753_pgfId-1003944]##A constructor that sets the _value_ field to
the passed parameter

[#50634753_pgfId-1028936]##A standard or generated holder class is
required to implement the marker _javax.xml.rpc.holders.Holder_
interface. The following code snippet shows the _Holder_ interface:

[#50634753_pgfId-1105500]##package _javax.xml.rpc.holders_ ;

[#50634753_pgfId-1105503]##public interface Holder \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1105501]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1097979]##A JAX-RPC implementation is required to
support serialization and deserialization of the value contained in a
_Holder_ class. This requirement holds for all types of _Holder_ classes
irrespective of whether a _Holder_ class is generated or is part of the
standard _javax.xml.rpc.holders_ package.

[#50634753_pgfId-1105525]##The following are the standard _Holder_
classes specified in the _javax.xml.rpc.holders_ package:

[#50634753_pgfId-1105528]## _BigDecimalHolder_

[#50634753_pgfId-1105529]## _BigIntegerHolder_

[#50634753_pgfId-1105530]## _BooleanHolder_

[#50634753_pgfId-1105548]## _BooleanWrapperHolder_

[#50634753_pgfId-1105531]## _ByteArrayHolder_

[#50634753_pgfId-1105532]## _ByteHolder_

[#50634753_pgfId-1105533]## _ByteWrapperHolder_

[#50634753_pgfId-1105534]## _CalendarHolder_

[#50634753_pgfId-1105535]## _DoubleHolder_

[#50634753_pgfId-1105536]## _DoubleWrapperHolder_

[#50634753_pgfId-1105537]## _FloatHolder_

[#50634753_pgfId-1105538]## _FloatWrapperHolder_

[#50634753_pgfId-1105539]## _IntHolder_

[#50634753_pgfId-1105540]## _IntegerWrapperHolder_

[#50634753_pgfId-1105541]## _LongHolder_

[#50634753_pgfId-1105542]## _LongWrapperHolder_

[#50634753_pgfId-1105543]## _ObjectHolder_

[#50634753_pgfId-1105544]## _QNameHolder_

[#50634753_pgfId-1105545]## _ShortHolder_

[#50634753_pgfId-1105546]## _ShortWrapperHolder_

[#50634753_pgfId-1105547]## _StringHolder_

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1003955]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1028939]##The following is an example of a _Holder_
class for a simple XML data type:

[#50634753_pgfId-1003959]##//Java

[#50634753_pgfId-1018668]##package javax.xml.rpc.holders;

[#50634753_pgfId-1029009]##public final class ShortHolder implements

[#50634753_pgfId-1003961]## public short value;

[#50634753_pgfId-1003967]##

[#50634753_pgfId-1003973]## }

[#50634753_pgfId-1018642]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1003956]##The following is an example of a Holder class

[#50634753_pgfId-1097114]##The following shows an example of an array

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1028208]##[#50634753_91875]##WSDL Fault

[#50634753_pgfId-1028209]##The _wsdl:fault_ element (an optional element
in a _wsdl:operation_ ) specifies the abstract message format for any
error messages that may be output as a result of a remote operation.
According to the WSDL specification, a fault message must have a single
part.

[#50634753_pgfId-1100880]##A _wsdl:fault_ is mapped to either a
_java.rmi.RemoteException_ (or its subclass), service specific Java
exception (described later in this section) or a _javax.xml.rpc_ .
_soap.SOAPFaultException_ . Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_50628[See SOAP Fault] for more details on the
Java mapping of a WSDL fault based on the SOAP binding.

[#50634753_pgfId-1100754]##Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_51680[See Mapping of Remote Exceptions] for the
mapping between the standard SOAP faults
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_65269[See W3C: SOAP 1.2:
http://www.w3.org/TR/2002/CR-soap12-part1-20021219/ and
http://www.w3.org/TR/2002/CR-soap12-part2-20021219/] and the
_java.rmi.RemoteException_ .

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1104367]##Service Specific Exception

[#50634753_pgfId-1104368]##A service specific Java exception (mapped
from a _wsdl:fault_ and the corresponding _wsdl:message_ ) extends the
class _java.lang.Exception_ directly or indirectly.

[#50634753_pgfId-1105363]##The single message part in the _wsdl:message_
(referenced from the _wsdl:fault_ element) may be either a type or an
element. If the former, it can be either a _xsd:complexType_ or a simple
XML type.

[#50634753_pgfId-1108179]##Each element inside the _xsd:complexType_ is
mapped to a getter method and a parameter in the constructor of the Java
exception. Mapping of these elements follows the standard XML to Java
type mapping. The name of the Java exception class is mapped from the
_name_ attribute of the _xsd:complexType_ for the single message part.
This naming scheme enables the WSDL to Java mapping to map an
_xsd:complexType_ derivation hierarchy to the corresponding Java
exception class hierarchy. The following section illustrates an example.
Refer to the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_96144[See XML Names] for the
mapping of XML names to Java identifiers.

[#50634753_pgfId-1105439]##If the single message part in the
_wsdl:message_ (referenced from the _wsdl:fault_ element) has a simple
XML type or array, then this element is mapped to a getter method and a
parameter in the constructor of the Java exception. In this case, the
_name_ of the Java exception class is mapped from the _name_ attribute
of the _wsdl:message_ element.

[#50634753_pgfId-1110103]##If the single message part in the
_wsdl:message_ refers to an element, then the type of that element is
used to derive the corresponding Java exception class using the rules in
the preceding paragraph.

[#50634753_pgfId-1110111]##The mapped service specific Java exception is
declared as a checked exception in the corresponding Java method mapping
for the _wsdl:operation_ element. This is in addition to the required
_java.rmi.RemoteException_ .

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1104374]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1104375]##The following shows an example of the mapping
of a _wsdl:fault_ to a service specific Java exception. The
_wsdl:message_ has a single _part_ of type _xsd:string_ :

[#50634753_pgfId-1104376]##<!-- WSDL Extract -->

[#50634753_pgfId-1104377]##<message name=”InvalidTickerException”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1104378]## <part name=”tickerSymbol”
type=”xsd:string”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1104379]##</message>

[#50634753_pgfId-1104380]##<portType name=”StockQuoteProvider”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1104381]## <operation name=”getLastTradePrice” ...>

[#50634753_pgfId-1104382]## <input message=”tns:getLastTradePrice”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1104383]## <output
message=”tns:getLastTradePriceResponse”/>

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1005945]##WSDL Binding

[#50634753_pgfId-1003913]##A _wsdl:binding_ defines concrete message
format and protocol binding for the abstract operations, messages and
port types specified in a WSDL document. An example of a binding is the
_soap:binding_ that defines a binding for SOAP 1.1 service ports.

[#50634753_pgfId-1004668]##The JAX-RPC specification does not define a
standard Java representation of the _wsdl:binding_ element.

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1009237]##WSDL Port

[#50634753_pgfId-1009238]##A _wsdl:port_ element specifies an address
for a service port (or endpoint) based on the specified protocol
binding. A _wsdl:port_ should have a unique name among all ports defined
within an enclosing WSDL document.

[#50634753_pgfId-1060109]##In the JAX-RPC service client programming
model, a service endpoint (defined using _wsdl:port_ ) is accessed using
an instance of a generated stub class, a dynamic proxy or a _Call_
object. Refer to the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_95029[See WSDL Service]
for details on how a stub instance and dynamic proxy are created.

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1060115]##[#50634753_95029]##WSDL Service

[#50634753_pgfId-1067502]##A _wsdl:service_ groups a set of service
endpoints (or ports), with each service endpoint defined with specific
port type, binding and endpoint address.

[#50634753_pgfId-1067503]##The JAX-RPC specification defines the mapping
of a _wsdl:service_ element to a service class. A service class acts as
a factory of the following:

[#50634753_pgfId-1067506]##Dynamic proxy for a service endpoint. Refer
to the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_72254[See Dynamic Proxy].

[#50634753_pgfId-1067508]##Instance of the type _javax.xml.rpc.Call_ for
the dynamic invocation of a remote operation on a service endpoint.
Refer to the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_87541[See DII Call Interface].

[#50634753_pgfId-1067514]##Instance of a generated stub class. Refer to
the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_34332[See Generated Stub Class].

[#50634753_pgfId-1067516]##A service class implements one of the
following interfaces:

[#50634753_pgfId-1067517]##The base _javax.xml.rpc.Service_ interface
directly, or,

[#50634753_pgfId-1067518]##A generated service interface. This service
interface is generated during the WSDL-to-Java mapping and extends the
base _javax.xml.rpc.Service_ interface. An example of a generated
service interface is _com.example.StockQuoteService_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1071525]##The following diagram shows the service
interface hierarchy.

image:jaxrpc-17.gif[image]

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1067540]##[#50634753_45908]##Service Interface

[#50634753_pgfId-1067541]##The following code snippet shows the
_javax.xml.rpc.Service_ interface:

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1067542]##javax.xml.rpc.Service interface

[#50634753_pgfId-1067543]##package javax.xml.rpc;

[#50634753_pgfId-1067544]##public interface Service \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1067546]## java.rmi.Remote getPort(QName portName,

[#50634753_pgfId-1067547]## Class serviceEndpointInterface)

[#50634753_pgfId-1067548]## throws ServiceException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1087022]## java.rmi.Remote getPort(Class
serviceEndpointInterface)

[#50634753_pgfId-1087023]## throws ServiceException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1091707]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1091717]## Call createCall() throws ServiceException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1091718]## Call createCall(QName portName) throws
ServiceException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1091719]## Call createCall(QName portName, String
operationName)

[#50634753_pgfId-1091720]## throws ServiceException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1091721]## Call createCall(QName portName, QName
operationName)

[#50634753_pgfId-1091722]## throws ServiceException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1103430]## Call[] getCalls(QName portName) throws
ServiceException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1091712]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1091713]## java.net.URL getWSDLDocumentLocation();

[#50634753_pgfId-1067556]## QName getServiceName();

[#50634753_pgfId-1067557]## java.util.Iterator getPorts() throws
ServiceException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1096800]## // ...

[#50634753_pgfId-1067558]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1073731]##A JAX-RPC runtime system is required to
provide the implementation class for the base _javax.xml.rpc.Service_
interface. This implementation class is required to support the creation
of both dynamic proxies and _Call_ objects.

[#50634753_pgfId-1073752]##The JAX-RPC specification does not specify
the design of a service implementation class. The base _Service_
interface is implemented in a vendor specific manner. For example, a
_Service_ implementation class may be created with a reference to an
in-memory representation of the WSDL service description.

[#50634753_pgfId-1073744]##The method _getPort_ ( _QName_ , Class)
returns a dynamic proxy or instance of a generated stub class for the
specified service endpoint. A JAX-RPC service client uses the returned
dynamic proxy or stub instance to invoke operations on the target
service endpoint. The parameter _serviceEndpointInterface_ specifies the
service endpoint interface that must be supported by the created dynamic
proxy or stub instance.

[#50634753_pgfId-1103389]##The method _getPort_ ( _Class_ ) returns
either an instance of a generated stub implementation class or a dynamic
proxy. The parameter _serviceEndpoint_ - Interface specifies the service
endpoint interface that is supported by the returned stub or proxy. In
the implementation of this method, the JAX-RPC runtime system takes the
responsibility of selecting a protocol binding (and a port) and
configuring the stub accordingly. The returned _Stub_ instance should
not be reconfigured by the client.

[#50634753_pgfId-1067562]##This _getPort_ method throws
_ServiceException_ if there is an error in the creation of a dynamic
proxy/stub instance or if there is any missing WSDL related metadata as
required by this method implementation.

[#50634753_pgfId-1103403]##The method _getPorts_ returns a list of
qualified names (as _javax.xml.namespace_ . _QName_ ) of ports grouped
by this service.

[#50634753_pgfId-1067563]##The multiple variants of the method
_createCall_ create instances of the _javax.xml. rpc.Call_ . Refer to
the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_87541[See DII Call Interface] and Javadocs
for more details on these methods. The _createCall_ method throws
_ServiceException_ if there is any error in the creation of the _Call_
object.

[#50634753_pgfId-1103499]##The _getCalls_ method returns an array of
preconfigured _Call_ objects for invoking operations on the specified
port. There is one _Call_ object per operation that can be invoked on
the specified port. A pre-configured _Call_ object does not need to be
configured using the setter methods on the _Call_ interface. Each
invocation of the _getCalls_ method is required to return a new array of
preconfigured _Call_ objects. This enables _Service_ implementation
class to avoid side effects of any setter methods that are invoked on
the returned _Call_ objects.

[#50634753_pgfId-1106062]##The _getCalls_ method requires the _Service_
implementation class to have access to the WSDL related metadata. This
method throws _ServiceException_ if this _Service_ instance does not
have access to the required WSDL metadata or if an illegal _portName_ is
specified.

[#50634753_pgfId-1103433]##The _Service_ implementation class should
implement _java.io.Serializable_ and/or _javax.naming.Referenceable_
interfaces to support registration in the JNDI namespace.

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1088992]##[#50634753_55177]##Generated Service

[#50634753_pgfId-1067571]##A WSDL to Java mapping tool is required to
generate a service interface based on the mapping of a _wsdl:service_
element in the WSDL document. This generated service interface is used
for the creation of instances of the generated stub classes.

[#50634753_pgfId-1096535]##A JAX-RPC runtime system is required to
provide the implementation class for the generated service interface.
The design of a generated service implementation class is specific to a
vendor’s implementation. A service implementation class should implement
_java.io.Serializable_ and/or _javax.naming.Referenceable_ interfaces to
support registration in the JNDI namespace.

[#50634753_pgfId-1067580]##A generated service interface is required to
follow the design pattern:

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1067581]##Design pattern for a generated service interface

[#50634753_pgfId-1067582]##public interface <ServiceName> extends
javax.xml.rpc.Service \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1067583]## <serviceEndpointInterface>
get<Name_of_wsdl:port>()

[#50634753_pgfId-1067584]## throws ServiceException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1067585]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1067586]## // ... Additional getter methods

[#50634753_pgfId-1067587]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1073781]##The name _<ServiceName>_ of the generated
service interface is mapped from the _name_ attribute of the
corresponding _wsdl:service_ definition. Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_96144[See XML Names] for the mapping of the XML
names to the Java identifiers.

[#50634753_pgfId-1067592]##For each _wsdl:port_ defined in a
_wsdl:service_ definition, the generated service interface contains the
following methods:

{empty}[#50634753_pgfId-1067593]##Required _get<Name_of_wsdl:port>_
method that takes no parameters and returns an instance of the stub
class that implements the _<_ serviceEndpointInterface _>_ interface.
The _<_ serviceEndpointInterface _>_ interface is mapped from the
_wsdl:portType_ and _wsdl:binding_ definitions for this _wsdl:port_ .
Refer to the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_43187[See WSDL Port Type]

[#50634753_pgfId-1067594]##Optional _get<Name_of_wsdl:port>_ methods
that include parameters specific to the endpoint (or port)
configuration. Each such getter method returns an instance of a
generated stub class that implements the _<_ serviceEndpointInterface
_>_ interface. An example is a getter method that takes security
information (example: user name, password) as parameters. These
additional getter methods are specific to a JAX-RPC implementation.

[#50634753_pgfId-1073876]##All _get<Name_of_wsdl:port>_ methods are
required to throw the _ServiceException_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1109482]##The name of the _get<Name_of_wsdl:port>_
methods is obtained by first mapping the name of the _wsdl:port_ to a
Java identifier according to the rules in section 4.1, “XML Names”, then
treating it as a JavaBean property name for the purpose of adding to it
the “get” prefix.

[#50634753_pgfId-1011088]##Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_98773[See J2EE based Service Client Programming
Model] for more details on the use of the generated service class.

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1091739]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1091742]##The following code snippet shows an example
of the generated service interface. This service interface is generated
using the WSDL example in the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_59165[See Service
Description]:

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1091744]##[#50634753_51386]##Example of a Generated Service Interface: StockQuoteService

[#50634753_pgfId-1091745]##package com.example;

[#50634753_pgfId-1091746]##public interface StockQuoteService extends
javax.xml.rpc.Service \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1091747]## StockQuoteProvider
getStockQuoteProviderPort()

[#50634753_pgfId-1097863]## throws ServiceException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1091748]## // ...

[#50634753_pgfId-1091749]##}

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1101894]##Name Collisions

[#50634753_pgfId-1101895]##Note that the WSDL 1.1 specification allows
various element definitions to have the same name within a specified
namespace in the WSDL document. This leads to potential name conflicts
in the WSDL to Java mapping. To address this issue, a WSDL to Java
mapping tool is required to resolve any potential name collisions.

[#50634753_pgfId-1101193]##The following table specifies rules for
avoiding name collisions in the WSDL to Java mapping. Suffixes are
appended to the mapped Java identifiers to resolve the name conflicts.
If there are no name collisions, there is no requirement to use these
suffixes.

[#50634753_pgfId-1103272]##
