== [#50634753_pgfId-1101254]##

image:jaxrpc-3.gif[image]

[#50634753_35315]##Java to XML/WSDL Mapping

image:jaxrpc-4.gif[image]

[#50634753_pgfId-1004841]##This chapter specifies the standard mapping
from the Java definitions to XML and WSDL definitions. This mapping
specifies the following:

[#50634753_pgfId-1067603]##Definition of a JAX-RPC supported Java type

[#50634753_pgfId-1045953]##Service endpoint interface for a JAX-RPC
service

[#50634753_pgfId-1019664]##Mapping from a Java service endpoint
definition to WSDL definitions

[#50634753_pgfId-1019668]##Mapping from the Java types to the XML data
types

[#50634753_pgfId-1020006]##Note that the JAX-RPC specification does not
require support for a round trip mapping between the WSDL and Java
definitions.

==== [#50634753_pgfId-1045458]##

image:jaxrpc-5.gif[image]

[#50634753_77963]##[#50634753_10169]##JAX-RPC Supported Java Types

[#50634753_pgfId-1067607]##The following are the JAX-RPC supported Java
types:

{empty}[#50634753_pgfId-1067611]##One of the Java primitive types as
specified in the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_74846[See Primitive Types]

{empty}[#50634753_pgfId-1067615]##A subset of the standard Java classes
(as specified in the J2SE APIs) as specified in the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_17783[See Standard Java Classes]

{empty}[#50634753_pgfId-1067628]##An array of a supported Java type as
specified in the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_46917[See Java Array]

{empty}[#50634753_pgfId-1067624]##An exception class as specified in the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_26883[See Service Specific Exception]

{empty}[#50634753_pgfId-1080632]##A JAX-RPC value type as specified in
the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_75215[See JAX-RPC Value Type]

[#50634753_pgfId-1045459]##A JAX-RPC runtime system implementation must
support transmission of the values of a JAX-RPC supported Java type
between a service client and service endpoint at runtime. Values of a
JAX-RPC supported Java type must be serializable to and from the
corresponding XML representation.

[#50634753_pgfId-1074097]##Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_44250[See Java to XML Type Mapping] for the XML
mapping of the JAX-RPC supported Java types.

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1067638]##[#50634753_74846]##Primitive Types

[#50634753_pgfId-1067639]##The JAX-RPC specification supports the
following Java primitive types and the corresponding wrapper Java
classes:

[#50634753_pgfId-1067640]## _boolean_ , _byte_ , _short_ , _int_ ,
_long_ , _float_ , _double_

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1067642]##[#50634753_46917]##Java Array

[#50634753_pgfId-1067643]##The JAX-RPC specification supports a Java
array with members of a supported JAX-RPC Java type. The JAX-RPC
specification requires support for Java array of type _java.lang.Object_
. Multidimensional Java arrays are also supported. Examples are _int[]_
and _String[][]_ .

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1067645]##[#50634753_17783]##Standard Java Classes

[#50634753_pgfId-1067646]##The following standard Java classes are
supported by JAX-RPC:

[#50634753_pgfId-1067647]## _java.lang.String_

[#50634753_pgfId-1067648]## _java.util.Date_

[#50634753_pgfId-1091809]##java.util.Calendar

[#50634753_pgfId-1067649]## _java.math.BigInteger_

[#50634753_pgfId-1067650]## _java.math.BigDecimal_

[#50634753_pgfId-1109907]##javax.xml.namespace.QName

[#50634753_pgfId-1109908]##java.net.URI

[#50634753_pgfId-1075101]##Other standard Java classes (for example:
classes in the Java Collection Framework) are mapped using pluggable
serializers and deserializers. Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_41163[See Extensible Type Mapping] for more
details on the pluggable serializers and deserializers.

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1084939]##JAX-RPC Value Type

[#50634753_pgfId-1084940]##Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_75215[See JAX-RPC Value Type] for more details.

==== [#50634753_pgfId-1004846]##

image:jaxrpc-5.gif[image]

[#50634753_36514]##JAX-RPC Service Endpoint Interface

[#50634753_pgfId-1004850]##The JAX-RPC specification requires that a
JAX-RPC service endpoint interface must follow the following rules:

[#50634753_pgfId-1042605]##Service endpoint interface must extend
_java.rmi.Remote_ either directly or indirectly

[#50634753_pgfId-1042606]##All methods in the interface must throw
_java.rmi.RemoteException_ . Methods may throw service specific
exceptions in addition to the _RemoteException_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1042607]##Method parameters and return types must be
the JAX-RPC supported Java types (refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_77963[See JAX-RPC Supported Java Types]). At
runtime, values of a supported Java type must be serializable to and
from the corresponding XML representation.

[#50634753_pgfId-1103277]##Holder classes may be used as method
parameters. These _Holder_ classes are either generated or those
packaged in the standard _javax.xml.rpc.holders_ package.

[#50634753_pgfId-1042608]##Service endpoint interface must not include
constant (as _public final static)_ declarations. WSDL 1.1 specification
does not define any standard representation for constants in a
_wsdl:portType_ definition.

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1004878]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1004886]##The following code extract shows an example
of a service endpoint interface:

[#50634753_pgfId-1004900]##// Java

[#50634753_pgfId-1005618]##package com.example;

[#50634753_pgfId-1004897]##public interface StockQuoteProvider extends
java.rmi.Remote \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1004889]## float getLastTradePrice(String tickerSymbol)

[#50634753_pgfId-1004890]## throws java.rmi.RemoteException,

[#50634753_pgfId-1019759]## com.example.InvalidTickerException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1004891]## public StockQuoteInfo getStockQuote(String
tickerSymbol)

[#50634753_pgfId-1004892]## throws java.rmi.RemoteException,

[#50634753_pgfId-1019758]## com.example.InvalidTickerException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1075061]##}

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1075071]##[#50634753_26883]##Service Specific Exception

[#50634753_pgfId-1075072]##A JAX-RPC service endpoint interface that
extends the _java.rmi.Remote_ interface may declare service specific
exceptions in a method signature in addition to the required
_java.rmi.RemoteException_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1075073]##A service specific exception declared in a
remote method signature must be a checked exception. It must extend
_java.lang.Exception_ either directly or indirectly but must not be a
_RuntimeException_ .

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1075074]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1075075]##The following is an example of a service
specific Java exception:

[#50634753_pgfId-1075076]##// Java

[#50634753_pgfId-1075077]##package com.example;

[#50634753_pgfId-1075078]##public interface StockQuoteProvider extends
java.rmi.Remote \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1075079]## float getLastTradePrice(String tickerSymbol)

[#50634753_pgfId-1075080]## throws RemoteException,

[#50634753_pgfId-1102985]## com.example.InvalidTickerException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1075081]## // ...

[#50634753_pgfId-1075082]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1075083]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1075084]##public class InvalidTickerException extends
java.lang.Exception \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1075085]## public InvalidTickerException(String
tickersymbol) \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1075086]## public String getTickerSymbol() \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1075087]##}

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1075062]##Remote Reference Passing

[#50634753_pgfId-1075063]##The JAX-RPC specification does not require
support for the passing or return of a remote reference across a remote
method invocation. The reason is that SOAP
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_65269[See W3C: SOAP 1.2:
http://www.w3.org/TR/2002/CR-soap12-part1-20021219/ and
http://www.w3.org/TR/2002/CR-soap12-part2-20021219/] specifies
object-by-reference as out of scope in both the 1.1 and 1.2 versions.
Any support for remote reference passing in the JAX-RPC would be
non-standard and hence constrain interoperability.

[#50634753_pgfId-1045847]##A service endpoint interface must not include
a remote reference as either a parameter or a return type. A Java array
or JAX-RPC value type must not include a remote reference as a contained
element.

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1045841]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1045864]##The following is an example of a
non-conforming service endpoint interface.

[#50634753_pgfId-1004951]##// Java

[#50634753_pgfId-1005617]##package com.example;

[#50634753_pgfId-1004964]##public interface StockBroker extends
java.rmi.Remote \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1004969]## // ... Remote methods not shown

[#50634753_pgfId-1004970]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1004963]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1004954]##public interface StockQuoteProvider extends
java.rmi.Remote \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1004960]## StockBroker getPreferredStockBroker()

[#50634753_pgfId-1019783]## throws java.rmi.RemoteException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1005493]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1005531]##In the above example, the return type for the
method _getPreferredStockBroker_ represents a remote reference to the
_StockBroker_ service endpoint.

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1004974]##Pass by Copy

[#50634753_pgfId-1004999]##The JAX-RPC specification requires support
for the pass by copy parameter passing mode for all parameters and
return values. This is similar to the parameter passing semantics
defined by Java RMI link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_86731[See RMI
specification:
http://java.sun.com/j2se/1.3/docs/guide/rmi/spec/rmiTOC.html].

[#50634753_pgfId-1019808]##The value of a parameter object is copied
before invoking a remote method on a JAX-RPC service. By default, only
non-static and non-transient fields are copied. For return value, a new
object is created in the calling virtual machine.

==== [#50634753_pgfId-1079113]##

image:jaxrpc-5.gif[image]

[#50634753_44250]##Java to XML Type Mapping

[#50634753_pgfId-1073898]##This section specifies the standard mapping
of the Java types to the XML data types.

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1073900]##[#50634753_15137]##Java Primitive types

[#50634753_pgfId-1073901]##The following table specifies the standard
mapping of the Java primitive types to the XML data types:

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1073904]##Mapping of the Java Primitive Types

[#50634753_pgfId-1073908]##Java Primitive Type

[#50634753_pgfId-1073910]##XML Data Type

[#50634753_pgfId-1073912]## _boolean_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073914]## _xsd:boolean_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073920]## _byte_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073922]## _xsd:byte_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073924]## _short_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073926]## _xsd:short_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073928]## _int_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073930]## _xsd:int_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073932]## _long_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073934]## _xsd:long_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073936]## _float_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073938]## _xsd:float_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073940]## _double_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073942]## _xsd:double_

[#50634753_pgfId-1074140]##In the case of literal element declarations,
the Java class for a Java primitive type (example: _java.lang.Integer_ )
is mapped to an element declaration with the _nillable_ attribute set to
_true_ and with the corresponding built-in XML data type. The following
example shows the mapping for the _java.lang.Integer_ :

[#50634753_pgfId-1093713]##<xsd:element name="code" type="xsd:int"
nillable="true"/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1093714]##<!-- Schema instance -->

[#50634753_pgfId-1093715]##<code xsi:nil="true"></code>

[#50634753_pgfId-1093720]##Note that the SOAP 1.1 specification
indicates that all SOAP encoded elements are _nillable_ . So in the SOAP
encoded case, the Java wrapper class for a Java primitive type is mapped
to the corresponding SOAP encoded type. For example, the
_java.lang.Integer_ maps to _soapenc:int_ if the SOAP encoding is being
used.

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1073972]##Standard Java Classes[#50634753_75412]##

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1073945]##Mapping of Standard Java Classes

[#50634753_pgfId-1073949]##Java Class

[#50634753_pgfId-1073951]##XML Data Type

[#50634753_pgfId-1073953]## _java.lang.String_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073955]## _xsd:string_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073957]## _java.math.BigInteger_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073959]## _xsd:integer_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073961]## _java.math.BigDecimal_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073963]## _xsd:decimal_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073965]## _java.util.Calendar_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073967]## _xsd:dateTime_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073969]## _java.util.Date_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073971]## _xsd:dateTime_

[#50634753_pgfId-1109901]##javax.xml.namespace.QName

[#50634753_pgfId-1109903]##xsd:QName

[#50634753_pgfId-1109897]##java.net.URI

[#50634753_pgfId-1109899]##xsd:anyURI

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1074154]##Array of Bytes

[#50634753_pgfId-1074156]##Both _byte[]_ and _Byte[]_ are mapped to the
_xsd:base64Binary_ type.

[#50634753_pgfId-1111394]##The mapping of the _java.lang.Byte[]_ type to
the _xsd:base64Binary_ type is now deprecated because it cannot
represent _null_ values accurately. Instead, _Byte[]_ should be mapped
to a regular array following the rules in
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_85366[See Java Array].

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1074155]##[#50634753_85366]##Java Array

[#50634753_pgfId-1073975]##The JAX-RPC specification maps a Java array
to one of the following XML types:

[#50634753_pgfId-1075427]##An array derived from the _soapenc:Array_
using the _wsdl:arrayType_ attribute for restriction. This case is
specified in the WSDL 1.1 link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_91453[See Web
Services Description Language (WSDL) 1.1: http://www.w3.org/TR/wsdl]
specification

[#50634753_pgfId-1073980]##An array with the _soapenc:arrayType_ in the
schema instance as specified in the SOAP 1.1 encoding

[#50634753_pgfId-1073981]##An array derived from the _soapenc:Array_ by
restriction as specified in the SOAP 1.1 specification

[#50634753_pgfId-1098229]##An element in a _xsd:complexType_ with the
_maxOccurs_ attribute set to an integer greater than 1 or _unbounded_ .
This is one form of mapping used for Java arrays defined in a JAX-RPC
value type. Refer to the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_75215[See JAX-RPC
Value Type] for more details on the JAX-RPC value types.

[#50634753_pgfId-1098220]##Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_83219[See Appendix: XML Schema Support] for
examples of the above cases.

[#50634753_pgfId-1073982]##The JAX-RPC specification requires support
for the mapping of the multi-dimensional Java arrays. The member type of
a Java array must be a JAX-RPC supported Java type as defined in the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_77963[See JAX-RPC Supported Java Types]. The
mapped XML array contains elements with XML data type mapped from the
corresponding member type of the Java array.

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1073986]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1073987]##// Java

[#50634753_pgfId-1073988]##int[] numbers;

[#50634753_pgfId-1073989]##The above Java array is mapped to the
following schema fragment:

[#50634753_pgfId-1073990]##<!-- Schema fragment -->

[#50634753_pgfId-1073991]## _<complexType name="numbers">_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073992]## _<complexContent>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073993]## _<restriction base="soapenc:Array">_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073994]## _<attribute ref="soapenc:arrayType"
wsdl:arrayType="xsd:int[]"/>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073995]## _</restriction>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073996]## _</complexContent>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073997]## _</complexType>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1073998]##The following example shows another form of
XML schema representation and an XML schema instance:

[#50634753_pgfId-1073999]##<!-- Schema fragment -->

[#50634753_pgfId-1074000]##<element name=”numbers”
type=”soapenc:Array”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1074001]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1074002]##<!-- Schema instance -->

[#50634753_pgfId-1074003]##<numbers soapenc:arrayType=”xsd:int[3]”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1074004]## <member>1</member>

[#50634753_pgfId-1074005]## <member>2</member>

[#50634753_pgfId-1074006]## <member>3</member>

[#50634753_pgfId-1074007]##</numbers>

==== [#50634753_pgfId-1080710]##

image:jaxrpc-5.gif[image]

[#50634753_75215]##[#50634753_33043]##JAX-RPC Value Type

[#50634753_pgfId-1095518]##This section specifies requirements for the
JAX-RPC value types.

[#50634753_pgfId-1095519]##A JAX-RPC value type is a Java class whose
value can be moved between a service client and service endpoint. A Java
class must follow these rules to be a JAX-RPC conformant value type:

[#50634753_pgfId-1080716]##Java class must have a public default
constructor.

[#50634753_pgfId-1080717]##Java class must not implement (directly or
indirectly) the _java.rmi.Remote_ interface.

[#50634753_pgfId-1080718]##Java class may implement any Java interface
(except the _java.rmi.Remote_ interface) or extend another Java class.

[#50634753_pgfId-1080719]##Java class may contain public, private,
protected, package-level fields. The Java type of a public field must be
a supported JAX-RPC type as specified in the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_77963[See JAX-RPC Supported Java Types].

[#50634753_pgfId-1080723]##Java class may contain methods. There are no
specified restrictions on the nature of these methods. Refer to the
later rule about the JavaBeans properties.

[#50634753_pgfId-1080724]##Java class may contain static or transient
fields.

[#50634753_pgfId-1095537]##Java class for a JAX-RPC value type may be
designed as a JavaBeans class. In this case, the bean properties (as
defined by the JavaBeans introspection) are required to follow the
JavaBeans design pattern of setter and getter methods. The Java type of
a bean property must be a supported JAX-RPC type as specified in the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_77963[See JAX-RPC Supported Java Types].

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1095541]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1080730]##The following code snippets show valid
examples of JAX-RPC value types:

[#50634753_pgfId-1080731]##// Java

[#50634753_pgfId-1080732]##public class Base \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1080733]## public Base() \{ }

[#50634753_pgfId-1080734]## public int a;

[#50634753_pgfId-1080735]## private int b;

[#50634753_pgfId-1080736]## private int c;

[#50634753_pgfId-1080737]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1080738]## public int getB() \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1080739]## return b;

[#50634753_pgfId-1080740]## }

[#50634753_pgfId-1080741]## public void setB(int b) \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1080742]## this.b = b;

[#50634753_pgfId-1080743]## }

[#50634753_pgfId-1080744]## public void someMethod() \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1080745]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1080746]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1080747]##public class Derived extends Base \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1080748]## public Derived() \{ }

[#50634753_pgfId-1080749]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1080750]## public int x;

[#50634753_pgfId-1080751]## private int y;

[#50634753_pgfId-1080752]##}

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1080754]##[#50634753_63973]##XML Mapping

[#50634753_pgfId-1080755]##A JAX-RPC value type is mapped to an
_xsd:complexType_ with either the _xsd:all_ or the _xsd:sequence_
compositor. Please notice that the XML Schema specification places
several restrictions on the contents of a particle that uses the
_xsd:all_ compositor.

[#50634753_pgfId-1111079]##The standard Java to XML mapping of a JAX-RPC
value type must follow these rules:

[#50634753_pgfId-1080756]##The _name_ attribute of the _xsd:complexType_
is mapped from the name of the Java class for the JAX-RPC value type.

[#50634753_pgfId-1080757]##Each public non-final non-transient field in
the Java class is mapped to an element in the _xsd:complexType._ The
_name_ and _type_ attributes of the mapped element are mapped from the
name and Java type of the public field. The _type_ attribute is derived
from the Java type of the public field using the type mapping rules in
the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_44250[See Java to XML Type Mapping].

[#50634753_pgfId-1080761]##Each read/write property (as identified by
the _java.beans.Introspector_ class) is mapped to an element in the
_xsd:complexType_ . The _name_ attribute for the mapped element is
derived from the name of the property. The _type_ attribute is mapped
from the Java type of the property using the type mapping specified in
the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_44250[See Java to XML Type Mapping].

[#50634753_pgfId-1080765]##Inheritance of the Java classes is mapped
using the derivation of _xsd:complexType_ types using the extension
mechanism.

[#50634753_pgfId-1080766]##The only fields that are mapped are the
non-transient, non-final public fields.

[#50634753_pgfId-1080767]##No methods are mapped.

[#50634753_pgfId-1098217]##There is no standard mapping of indexed
properties as reported by the JavaBeans introspection.

[#50634753_pgfId-1080769]##There is no standard mapping for the case
when a JavaBean property has the same name as a public field. A Java to
XML mapping implementation is required to flag this case as an error.

[#50634753_pgfId-1080770]##Note that the pluggable serializers and
deserializers may be used to support an advanced custom form of mapping
for the JAX-RPC value types. Such custom mapping may add implementation
specific additional rules over the above standard XML mapping.

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1080771]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1080772]##The XML mapping for the _Base_ class is as
shown below:

[#50634753_pgfId-1080773]##<complexType name="Base">

[#50634753_pgfId-1080774]## <sequence>

[#50634753_pgfId-1080775]## <element name="a" type="xsd:int"/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1080776]## <element name="b" type="xsd:int"/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1080777]## </sequence>

[#50634753_pgfId-1080778]##</complexType>

[#50634753_pgfId-1080779]##The _Base_ XML type includes elements based
on the mapping of the public field _a_ and the bean property _b_ (mapped
from the pair of _getB_ and _setB_ methods). The private field _c_ and
the method _someMethod_ are not mapped.

[#50634753_pgfId-1080780]##The _Derived_ class is mapped to the
following XML schema type:

[#50634753_pgfId-1080781]##<complexType name="Derived">

[#50634753_pgfId-1080782]## <complexContent>

[#50634753_pgfId-1080783]## <extension base="Base">

[#50634753_pgfId-1080784]## <sequence>

[#50634753_pgfId-1080785]## <element name="x" type="xsd:int"/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1080786]## </sequence>

[#50634753_pgfId-1080787]## </extension>

[#50634753_pgfId-1080788]## </complexContent>

[#50634753_pgfId-1080789]##</complexType>

[#50634753_pgfId-1080790]##The _Derived_ XML type extends from the
_Base_ type. The _Derived_ XML type includes element _x_ mapped from the
public field _x_ in the _Derived_ Java class. The private field _y_ in
the _Derived_ class is not mapped.

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1080792]##Java [#50634753_57839]##Serialization Semantics

[#50634753_pgfId-1095445]##The default serialization semantics (termed
SOAP serialization semantics) and on-wire representation of a JAX-RPC
value type are defined in terms of the XML mapping of a JAX-RPC value
type. Based on the standard XML mapping of a JAX-RPC value type (as
defined in the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_63973[See XML Mapping]), the
default serialized state for a JAX-RPC value type includes only the XML
mapping of the public fields and bean properties. For example, the
serialized state for the _Base_ value type includes only the public
field _a_ and property _b_ . This XML serialized state gets transmitted
over the wire between the client and service.

[#50634753_pgfId-1080798]##The XML/SOAP serialization semantics and
representation for a JAX-RPC value type differ from the standard Java
serialization. In the standard Java serialization, the serialized state
includes the public, private, protected and package level non-transient
fields for a serializable Java class. RMI-IIOP uses the standard Java
serialization semantics for its value types.

[#50634753_pgfId-1080799]##A JAX-RPC value type is required to conform
to the following set of rules if a JAX-RPC value type requires the Java
serialization semantics. Note that the following rules are in addition
to the rules (in the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_33043[See JAX-RPC Value
Type]) for a JAX-RPC value type:

[#50634753_pgfId-1095480]##A JAX-RPC value type must implement the
_java.io.Serializable_ interface

[#50634753_pgfId-1080804]##All public fields in the Java class must be
non-transient.

[#50634753_pgfId-1080805]##Each non-public, non-transient field must
exactly represent a JavaBeans property, and vice versa.

[#50634753_pgfId-1088045]##Each non-public field that does not exactly
represent a JavaBeans property must be marked transient.

[#50634753_pgfId-1095497]##A JAX-RPC value type that conforms to the
above rules is usable across both JAX-RPC (with different protocol
bindings) and RMI-IIOP (that uses the standard Java serialization
semantics for its value types) with the same Java serialization
semantics.

[#50634753_pgfId-1096458]##A JAX-RPC value type that implements the
_Serializable_ interface but does not conform to all above rules, may
not have the Java serialization semantics.

==== [#50634753_pgfId-1005238]##

image:jaxrpc-5.gif[image]

[#50634753_40474]##Java to WSDL Mapping

[#50634753_pgfId-1042314]##This section specifies the standard mapping
of a JAX-RPC service endpoint definition to a WSDL service description.

[#50634753_pgfId-1042985]##Note that the Java to WSDL mapping specifies
mapping of the Java definitions to the abstract WSDL definitions
(namely: _wsdl:types_ , _wsdl:message_ , _wsdl:operation_ and
_wsdl:portType_ ). The following mapping specification does not specify
how the SOAP binding (or binding for any other protocol) is defined in a
WSDL document.

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1005245]##Java Identifier

[#50634753_pgfId-1071334]##A Java identifier is mapped to an equivalent
XML name. Java identfiers are legal XML names. Note that the SOAP 1.2
specification link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_65269[See W3C: SOAP 1.2:
http://www.w3.org/TR/2002/CR-soap12-part1-20021219/ and
http://www.w3.org/TR/2002/CR-soap12-part2-20021219/] specifies rules for
mapping application defined names to XML names.

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1005246]##Java Package

[#50634753_pgfId-1005261]##A Java package is mapped to a WSDL document.
The mapped WSDL document contains abstract definitions (port type,
operations, messages) based on the mapping of Java declarations in the
corresponding Java package.

[#50634753_pgfId-1005386]##The JAX-RPC specification requires the
namespace definitions in the WSDL document to be mapped in an
application specific manner. A Java to WSDL mapping tool is required to
support the configuration of the namespace definitions in the mapped
WSDL document.

[#50634753_pgfId-1020338]##Note that the Java to WSDL mapping
specification does not require any specific authoring style for the
mapped WSDL document. For example, the mapped WSDL definitions may be
separated into multiple WSDL documents that are imported across
documents.

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1005247]##[#50634753_35421]##Service Endpoint Interface

[#50634753_pgfId-1005385]##A service endpoint interface (that extends
_java.rmi.Remote_ ) is mapped to the _wsdl:portType_ element. The _name_
attribute of the _wsdl:portType_ has the same name as the service
endpoint interface.

[#50634753_pgfId-1005398]##Methods defined in a service endpoint
interface are mapped to the _wsdl:operation_ definitions in the
corresponding _wsdl:portType_ . Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_34399[See Methods] for more details on the
mapping of methods in a service endpoint interface.

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1005423]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1005426]##The following shows an example of a service
endpoint interface:

[#50634753_pgfId-1005474]##// Java

[#50634753_pgfId-1005612]##package com.example;

[#50634753_pgfId-1005462]##public interface StockQuoteProvider extends
java.rmi.Remote \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1005463]## float getLastTradePrice(String tickerSymbol)

[#50634753_pgfId-1005464]## throws java.rmi.RemoteException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1005465]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1005427]##The above service endpoint interface is
mapped to the following _wsdl:portType_ definition. Note that the
_parameterOrder_ attribute is optional based on the WSDL 1.1
specification:

[#50634753_pgfId-1005434]##<!-- WSDL extract -->

[#50634753_pgfId-1005611]##<portType name=”StockQuoteProvider”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1005435]## <operation name=”getLastTradePrice”

[#50634753_pgfId-1005436]## parameterOrder=”tickerSymbol”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1005437]## <input message=”tns:getLastTradePrice”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1005438]## <output
message=”tns:getLastTradePriceResponse”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1005496]## </operation>

[#50634753_pgfId-1005440]##</portType>

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1005514]##Inherited Service Endpoint interfaces

[#50634753_pgfId-1019992]##Each Java interface in the service endpoint
inheritance hierarchy is mapped to an equivalent _wsdl:portType_
definition. Since the WSDL 1.1 specification does not define a standard
representation for the inheritance of the _wsdl:portType_ elements, each
mapped _wsdl:portType_ definition includes mapping of the complete set
of inherited Java methods. The support for this mapping is optional.

[#50634753_pgfId-1106963]##The following example illustrates this
mapping.

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1005553]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1020043]##In the following example, the service
endpoint interfaces _StockQuoteProvider_ and _PremiumStockQuoteProvider_
are mapped to respective _wsdl:portType_ definitions. The port type
_StockQuoteProvider_ includes a single operation _getLastTradePrice_ ;
while the port type _PremiumStockQuoteProvider_ includes two operations
_getLastTradePrice_ and _getRealtimeLastTradePrice_ . The
_getLastTradePrice_ operation in the _PremiumStockQuoteProvider_ port
type is mapped from the corresponding inherited method.

[#50634753_pgfId-1005607]##// Java Code

[#50634753_pgfId-1005606]##package com.example;

[#50634753_pgfId-1005554]##public interface StockQuoteProvider extends
java.rmi.Remote \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1005581]## // gets a 20 minute delayed stock price

[#50634753_pgfId-1005555]## float getLastTradePrice(String tickerSymbol)

[#50634753_pgfId-1005556]## throws java.rmi.RemoteException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1005557]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1005560]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1005563]##package com.example;

[#50634753_pgfId-1005564]##public interface PremiumStockQuoteProvider
extends

[#50634753_pgfId-1005576]## com.example.StockQuoteProvider \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1045981]## // gets a realtime stock quote

[#50634753_pgfId-1045986]## float getRealtimeLastTradePrice(String
tickerSymbol)

[#50634753_pgfId-1005566]## throws java.rmi.RemoteException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1005567]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1020056]##The mapping of the _StockQuoteProvider_
interface is the same as shown in the example in the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_35421[See Service Endpoint Interface].

[#50634753_pgfId-1020057]##The _PremiumStockQuoteProvider_ interface is
mapped to the following _wsdl: portType_ definition:

[#50634753_pgfId-1020088]##<!-- WSDL Extract -->

[#50634753_pgfId-1020058]##<portType name=”PremiumStockQuoteProvider”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1020059]## <operation name=”getLastTradePrice”

[#50634753_pgfId-1020060]## parameterOrder=”tickerSymbol”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1020061]## <input message=”tns:getLastTradePrice”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1020062]## <output
message=”tns:getLastTradePriceResponse”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1020063]## </operation>

[#50634753_pgfId-1020116]## <operation name=”getRealtimeLastTradePrice”

[#50634753_pgfId-1020117]## parameterOrder=”tickerSymbol”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1020118]## <input
message=”tns:getRealtimeLastTradePrice”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1020119]## <output
message=”tns:getRealtimeLastTradePriceResponse”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1020120]## </operation>

[#50634753_pgfId-1020064]##</portType>

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1046189]##[#50634753_34399]##Methods

[#50634753_pgfId-1005384]##Each method on a Java service endpoint
interface is mapped to an equivalent _wsdl:operation_ definition. The
mapped _wsdl:operation_ definition preserves the method signature in
terms of the parameter ordering.

[#50634753_pgfId-1042193]##The standard mapping of a Java method to a
_wsdl:operation_ definitions follows these rules:

[#50634753_pgfId-1097517]##The _name_ attribute of the mapped
_wsdl:operation_ is the same as the name of the Java method.

[#50634753_pgfId-1098138]##Overloaded Java methods are mapped to
multiple _wsdl:operation_ elements. These mapped _wsdl:operation_
elements are named the same (as the name of the overloaded Java methods)
or with unique names depending on the mechanism that is used by the
server-side JAX-RPC runtime system to dispatch methods to the target
service endpoint. For example, a JAX-RPC runtime system may use unique
operation names, _SOAPAction_ or an implementation specific mechanism to
dispatch methods to the target service endpoint. Note that the JAX-RPC
specification does not require use of the _SOAPAction_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1073545]##A mapped _wsdl:operation_ contains
_wsdl:input_ and, unless it is one-way, _wsdl:output_ and optional
_wsdl:fault_ (s) based on the mapping of the Java method signature. The
_message_ attribute of these _wsdl:input_ and _wsdl:output_ elements
uses the qualified name of the corresponding _wsdl:message_ definition.
Only Java methods with a _void_ return type and that do not throw any
exception other than _java.rmi.RemoteException_ can be mapped to one-way
operations. Since not all Java methods that fulfill this requirement are
amenable to become one-way operations, Java to WSDL mapping tools are
required to provide a facility for specifying metadata used to identify
which of the methods should indeed be mapped to one-way operations.

[#50634753_pgfId-1042197]##Each Java parameter (in the Java method
signature) is mapped to a message part in the _wsdl:message_ . This
_wsdl:message_ corresponds to the _wsdl:input_ element for the mapped
_wsdl:operation_ . Each message part has a _name_ attribute that is
mapped based on the name of the Java parameter and a _type_ attribute
(an XML data type) mapped from the Java type of the parameter. Message
parts appear in the same order as in the Java method signature.

[#50634753_pgfId-1073564]##Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_89214[See Operation Style attribute] for the
requirements related to the mapping of Java methods to the
_soap:operation_ definitions with _document_ and _rpc_ styles in the
SOAP binding.

[#50634753_pgfId-1042201]##Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_43535[See Literal Representation] for details
related to the literal representation of SOAP messages for RPC calls and
responses. In brief, if literal representation is used for the SOAP
message, each message part in the SOAP body references a concrete schema
definition using either the _element_ or _type_ attribute. If the
_element_ attribute is used, the element referenced by the part appears
under the Body element. If the _type_ attribute is used, then the
referenced type becomes the schema type of the element.

[#50634753_pgfId-1042202]##A Java return type (for a Java method) is
mapped to a message part in the _wsdl:message_ . This _wsdl:message_
corresponds to the _wsdl:output_ element for the mapped
_wsdl:operation._ The _name_ of this message part is not significant.

[#50634753_pgfId-1103311]##For _Holder_ classes used as method
parameters, a Java to WSDL mapping tool is required to provide a
facility for specifying the related mapping metadata. This metadata
identifies whether a _Holder_ parameter in the method signature is
mapped to either the _OUT_ or _INOUT_ parameter mode. A mapping tool may
choose to map all _Holder_ parameters to the default _INOUT_ parameter
mode. Future versions of the JAX-RPC specification would consider
specifying a standard approach for specifying such mapping metadata.

[#50634753_pgfId-1042212]##Ordering of Java parameters is represented in
the _parameterOrder_ attribute in the _wsdl:operation_ element. The
message part for a return value is not listed in the _parameterOrder_
attribute. Refer to the WSDL 1.1 specification for more details on the
_parameterOrder_ attribute.

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1100931]##Exceptions

[#50634753_pgfId-1105178]##Each service specific Java exception in a
remote method signature is mapped to a _wsdl:fault_ element. This
_wsdl:fault_ element references a _wsdl:message_ element.

[#50634753_pgfId-1105176]##The _name_ attribute of the _wsdl:message_
element is the same as the name of the Java exception. The _message_
attribute of the _wsdl:fault_ element is the qualified name of the
_wsdl:message_ definition.

[#50634753_pgfId-1110026]##The single message part in the _wsdl:fault_
element (as required by the WSDL 1.1 specification) can refer to either
a type or an element. If it refers to a type, it is either a
_xsd:simpleType_ or a _xsd:complexType_ . If the latter, the _name_
attribute of the _xsd:complexType_ is the same as the name of the Java
exception class. Similarly, if it refers to an element, the _name_
attribute of the _xsd:element_ is the same as the name of the Java
exception class and its type must follow the rules for the mapping to
complex types given in this same section.

[#50634753_pgfId-1110024]##Multiple fields (each with a getter method
and corresponding parameter in the constructor) in the Java exception
class are mapped to elements of the _xsd:complexType_ . The _name_ and
_type_ attribute of each element are mapped from the name and Java type
of the corresponding field in the Java exception class. The mapping of
these fields follows the mapping specified in the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_44250[See Java to XML Type Mapping].

[#50634753_pgfId-1105579]##If a Java exception class has a single field
(with a getter method and corresponding parameter in the constructor),
this field is mapped (as an option to the previous bullet) to a single
message part in the _wsdl:message_ . The _name_ and _type_ of this
message _part_ are mapped from the name of Java type of the
corresponding field.

[#50634753_pgfId-1105567]##The _wsdl:message_ part represents the
contents of the _detail_ element in the SOAP fault.

[#50634753_pgfId-1105248]##Inheritance of Java exceptions is mapped
using the derivation of _xsd:complexType_ using the extension mechanism.
This applies to the _xsd:complexType_ used to represent the single
message _part_ in the _wsdl:message_ for the _wsdl:fault_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1046158]##A remote exception (
_java.rmi.RemoteException_ or its subclasses) is mapped to a standard
SOAP fault. Refer to the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_51680[See Mapping of
Remote Exceptions] for the standard mapping of remote exceptions.

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1046163]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1046164]##The following shows an example of a service
endpoint interface _StockQuoteProvider_ with a single method
_getLastTradePrice_ :

[#50634753_pgfId-1005721]##// Java

[#50634753_pgfId-1005722]##package com.example;

java.rmi.Remote \{

== [#50634753_pgfId-1090523]##

image:jaxrpc-3.gif[image]

[#50634753_75805]##SOAP Binding

image:jaxrpc-4.gif[image]

[#50634753_pgfId-1090524]##This chapter specifies the JAX-RPC support
for the SOAP 1.1 binding.

[#50634753_pgfId-1090525]##Note that this section uses extracts from the
WSDL 1.1 specification. In all cases, WSDL specification should override
any WSDL extracts that have been used in this chapter.

==== [#50634753_pgfId-1090527]##

image:jaxrpc-5.gif[image]

[#50634753_63057]##SOAP Binding in WSDL

[#50634753_pgfId-1090528]##The _soap:binding_ element in the WSDL
identifies that the SOAP protocol is used for binding the abstract WSDL
definitions.

[#50634753_pgfId-1090529]##The JAX-RPC specification requires support
for the following cases (termed _operation_ _modes_ ) for an operation
with the SOAP binding. Later sections of this chapter specify more
details on these supported operation modes:

[#50634753_pgfId-1090530]##Operation with the _rpc_ style and _encoded_
use ( _rpc/encoded_ )

[#50634753_pgfId-1109912]##Operation with the _rpc_ style and _literal_
use ( _rpc/literal_ )

[#50634753_pgfId-1090531]##Operation with the _document_ style and
_literal_ use ( _document/literal_ )

[#50634753_pgfId-1090536]##Refer to the WSDL 1.1
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_91453[See Web Services Description Language
(WSDL) 1.1: http://www.w3.org/TR/wsdl] specification for more details on
the _document_ and _rpc_ operation styles.

[#50634753_pgfId-1090537]##A JAX-RPC implementation is required to
support the above operation modes for the mapping of a WSDL based
service description to the corresponding Java representation.

[#50634753_pgfId-1090538]##A JAX-RPC implementation may choose to
support the optional operation mode of _document_ / _encoded_ .

==== [#50634753_pgfId-1090541]##

image:jaxrpc-5.gif[image]

[#50634753_89214]##Operation Style attribute

[#50634753_pgfId-1090542]##The _style_ attribute (specified per
_soap:operation_ element or as a default in the _soap:binding_ element)
indicates whether an operation is _rpc_ or _document_ oriented. In the
JAX-RPC programming model, both _rpc_ and _document_ style operations
are mapped to the corresponding remote methods on a service endpoint
interface.

[#50634753_pgfId-1090556]##A JAX-RPC client side implementation is
required to support use of services that follow either the WSDL 1.1 or
JAX-RPC (refer to the beginning of this section) specified _document_
and _rpc_ operation style requirements. Note that the WSDL 1.1
specification does not require a wrapper element for the _document_
style operations and assumes the use of _SOAPAction_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1090557]##The JAX-RPC specification requires that the
above requirements based on the operation style should be hidden from
the JAX-RPC programming model. A JAX-RPC implementation should take the
responsibility for the appropriate representation of a SOAP message
based on the operation style.

==== [#50634753_pgfId-1090559]##

image:jaxrpc-5.gif[image]

[#50634753_53899]##Encoded Representation

[#50634753_pgfId-1090560]##The JAX-RPC specification requires support
for _rpc_ style operations with the _encoded_ use. Support for
_document_ style operations with _encoded_ use is optional. In the
_encoded_ use, each message part in the SOAP body references an abstract
type using the _type_ attribute. These types are serialized according to
the encodings identified in the _encodingStyle_ attribute of the
_soap:body_ element. An example of such encoding is the SOAP 1.1
encoding link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_73033[See W3C Note: SOAP 1.1:
http://www.w3.org/TR/SOAP/].

[#50634753_pgfId-1090567]##Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_24046[See Interoperability] for the related
interoperability requirements.

==== [#50634753_pgfId-1090569]##

image:jaxrpc-5.gif[image]

[#50634753_43535]##Literal Representation

[#50634753_pgfId-1090570]##The JAX-RPC specification requires support
for _rpc_ and _document_ style operations with the _literal_ use. Note
that the _literal_ use is defined on the _soap:body_ element in the
WSDL.

[#50634753_pgfId-1090571]##If the use is _literal_ , each message part
in the SOAP Body element references a concrete schema definition using
either the _element_ or _type_ attribute. If the _element_ attribute is
used, the element referenced by the message part appears under the Body
element (with or without wrapper depending on the operation style). If
the _type_ attribute is used, the type referenced by the part becomes
the schema type of the enclosing element (Body element for the
_document_ style or part accessor element for the _rpc_ style). WSDL 1.1
specification allows (but does not require) use of an optional
_encodingStyle_ attribute for encoding in the literal case.

[#50634753_pgfId-1090572]##The JAX-RPC specification requires support
for the _element_ attribute in a message part with literal
representation and referenced by a _document_ style operation. It also
requires support for the _type_ attribute in a message part with literal
representation and referenced by an _rpc_ style operation. However, use
of any specific encoding style with the literal mode is not required. A
JAX-RPC implementation may use the optional _encodingStyle_ attribute
(in a _soap:body_ element with the _literal_ use) to apply specific
encoding rules.

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1090573]##[#50634753_61828]##Java Mapping of Literal Representation

[#50634753_pgfId-1090574]##The Java mapping for a message part (either a
parameter or return value) with literal representation depends on
whether the JAX-RPC specifies a standard Java mapping for the XML type
of this message part. The link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_83219[See Appendix:
XML Schema Support] specifies a subset of the XML schema data types that
a JAX-RPC implementation is required to support. Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_19087[See XML to Java Type Mapping] for the
specified mapping of this subset of XML schema.

[#50634753_pgfId-1109985]##When mapping _document_ style operations, in
addition to the regular mapping, JAX-RPC implementations are required to
support the so-called “wrapper” style, in which the logical parameters
of an operation are wrapped inside a _xsd:sequence_ element named after
the operation.

[#50634753_pgfId-1111487]##In order to qualify as using the “wrapper”
style, an operation must fulfill the following conditions:

[#50634753_pgfId-1111465]##its input and output messages (if present)
must contain exactly one part;

[#50634753_pgfId-1111476]##such a part must refer to an element named
after the operation;

[#50634753_pgfId-1111488]##such an element (a wrapper) must be of a
complex type defined using the _xsd:sequence_ compositor and containing
only elements declarations.

[#50634753_pgfId-1111498]##In this case, implementations must be able to
discard the wrapper elements and treat their children as the actual
parameters of the operation. Please refer to
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_15657[See Example] below for an example.

[#50634753_pgfId-1090581]##If there is no standard Java mapping for an
XML schema type, a message part with literal representation is
considered and mapped as a document fragment. The XML to Java mapping
uses the interface _javax.xml.soap.SOAPElement_ to represent a literal
message part in the Java mapping of a _wsdl:operation_ element. For
example, a parameter or a return type (for a remote operation)
represented as a literal message part is mapped to a _SOAPElement_ in
the Java method signature.

[#50634753_pgfId-1090582]##When a _SOAPElement_ is declared and passed
as parameter to the remote method call, the JAX-RPC runtime system
implementation is required to embed the XML representation of the
_SOAPElement_ instance as part of the underlying SOAP message
representation. This embedding of _SOAPElement_ instance is internal to
the implementation of a JAX-RPC runtime system.

[#50634753_pgfId-1109924]##In order to make it possible to use other
data binding frameworks (e.g. JAXB) in conjunction with JAX-RPC, it must
be possible to selectively turn the standard JAX-RPC type mapping off on
a per-part basis and revert to the default mapping, namely _SOAPElement_
. JAX-RPC tools are required to provide a facility to specify metadata
for this purpose.

[#50634753_pgfId-1090586]##Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_97255[See SOAPElement] for more details on the
_SOAPElement_ API.

[#50634753_pgfId-1090587]##Any other form of mapping between the Java
and XML data types for an operation with the literal use is specific to
a JAX-RPC implementation. A portable application should not rely on any
non-standard JAX-RPC implementation specific mapping. For example, a
JAX-RPC implementation may use a Java framework for XML data type
binding to map the literal parts. In this case, each literal part or its
elements is represented by an instance of a Java class generated by the
data binding framework. In the JAX-RPC specification, this form of
mapping is specific to a JAX-RPC implementation. Note that the JAXB 1.0
specification is defining standard Java APIs for the XML data binding.
Future versions of the JAX-RPC specification will consider use of the
JAXB 1.0 APIs.

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1090589]##[#50634753_97255]##SOAPElement

[#50634753_pgfId-1090590]##The following code snippet shows the
_javax.xml.soap.SOAPFactory_ . A _SOAPFactory_ is used to create a
_SOAPElement_ , _Detail_ and _Name_ objects. Refer to the JAXM 1.1 and
SAAJ link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_22105[See JAXM specification:
http://java.sun.com/xml/jaxm/] specification for complete details on the
_SOAPFactory_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1106675]##package javax.xml.soap;

[#50634753_pgfId-1106676]##public abstract class SOAPFactory \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1106677]## public abstract SOAPElement
createElement(Name name)

[#50634753_pgfId-1106678]## throws SOAPException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1106679]## public abstract SOAPElement
createElement(String localName)

[#50634753_pgfId-1106680]## throws SOAPException;

createElement(String localName,

[#50634753_pgfId-1106682]## String prefix, String uri)

[#50634753_pgfId-1106683]## throws SOAPException;

SOAPException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1106685]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1106686]## public abstract Name createName(String
localName,

[#50634753_pgfId-1106687]## String prefix, String uri)throws
SOAPException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1106688]## public abstract Name createName(String
localName)

[#50634753_pgfId-1106689]## throws SOAPException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1106690]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1106691]## public static SOAPFactory newInstance()

[#50634753_pgfId-1106692]## throws SOAPException \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1090603]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1090604]##The _SOAPFactory_ in the _javax.xml.soap_
package follows the abstract factory pattern. An instance of the
_SOAPFactory_ is created using the static _newInstance_ method.

[#50634753_pgfId-1090605]##The variants of the _createElement_ method
create a _SOAPElement_ . The created _SOAPElement_ instance represents a
document fragment and can be used as parameter to a remote method call.
The JAX-RPC specification requires the use of the _SOAPFactory_ to
create _SOAPElement_ instances that are passed in the remote method
invocation.

[#50634753_pgfId-1090606]##The method _createName_ creates an instance
of the _javax.xml.soap.Name_ . The method _createDetail_ creates an
instance of the _javax.xml.soap.Detail_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1106695]##The following code snippet shows the
_javax.xml.soap.SOAPElement_ interface. This interface is used to
represent a literal message part when mapped as a document fragment.

[#50634753_pgfId-1090610]##Refer to the JAXM and SAAJ specifications
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_22105[See JAXM specification:
http://java.sun.com/xml/jaxm/] for complete details on the _SOAPElement_

[#50634753_pgfId-1090646]##A _SOAPElement_ instance represents the
contents in the SOAP Body element for either an RPC request or response.
Once a new _SOAPElement_ is created using the _SOAPFactory_ , the
various add methods are used to populate this document fragment.

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1090647]##[#50634753_15657]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1090648]##The following shows schema fragment for this
example. Let the namespace prefix be “ _s_ ” for the following schema
definitions:

[#50634753_pgfId-1090649]##<types>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090650]##<schema attributeFormDefault=”qualified”

[#50634753_pgfId-1090651]## elementFormDefault=”qualified”

[#50634753_pgfId-1090652]## targetNamespace=”...”>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090653]##<element name="DoExample">

[#50634753_pgfId-1090654]## <complexType>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090655]## <sequence>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090656]## <element name="value1" type="xsd:string"/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090657]## <element name="value2" type="xsd:string"/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090658]## </sequence>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090659]## </complexType>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090660]##</element>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090661]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1090662]##<element name="DoAnotherExample">

[#50634753_pgfId-1090663]## <complexType>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090664]## <sequence>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090665]## <element name="field1" type="xsd:string"/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090666]## <element name="field2" type="xsd:string"/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090667]## _... Other elements with types that do not
have standard mapping_

[#50634753_pgfId-1090668]## _... defined by JAX-RPC_

[#50634753_pgfId-1090669]## _</sequence>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1090670]## _<attribute name="generic" type="xsd:string"
use="required"/>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1090671]## _<anyAttribute namespace="##other”/>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1090672]## _</complexType>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1090673]## _</element>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1090674]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1090675]## _<element name="DoExampleResponse">_

[#50634753_pgfId-1109998]## <complexType>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090676]## _<sequence>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1109997]## <element name=”result” type=”xsd:string”/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1109996]## </sequence>

[#50634753_pgfId-1109999]## </complexType>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090677]## _</element>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1090678]## _</schema>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1090679]## _</types>_

[#50634753_pgfId-1090680]##The following WSDL extract shows the
definitions for the messages, port type and binding:

[#50634753_pgfId-1090681]##<!-- WSDL extract -->

[#50634753_pgfId-1090682]##<message name="DoExample">

[#50634753_pgfId-1090684]##</message>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090694]## <input message="tns:DoExample"/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090695]## <output message="tns:DoExampleResponse"/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090696]## </operation>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090698]## <input message="tns:DoAnotherExample"/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090699]## <output message="tns:DoExampleResponse"/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090700]## </operation>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090702]##...

type="tns:ExampleSoap">

[#50634753_pgfId-1090704]##<soap:binding style="document"

[#50634753_pgfId-1090705]##
transport="http://schemas.xmlsoap.org/soap/http"/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090706]##<operation name="DoExample">

[#50634753_pgfId-1090707]##<soap:operation soapAction=""
style="document"/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090708]## <input message="tns:DoExample">

[#50634753_pgfId-1090709]## <soap:body use="literal" parts="body"
namespace="..."/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090710]## </input>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090711]## <output message="tns:DoExampleResponse">

[#50634753_pgfId-1090712]## <soap:body use="literal" parts="result"
namespace="..."/>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090713]## </output>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090714]##</operation>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090715]##<operation name="DoAnotherExample">

[#50634753_pgfId-1090716]## ... same for the operation DoAnotherExample

[#50634753_pgfId-1090717]##</operation>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090718]##</binding>

[#50634753_pgfId-1090719]##The above example uses _document_ style and
_literal_ use.

[#50634753_pgfId-1090726]##Based on the specification in the sections
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_89214[See Operation Style attribute] and
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_43535[See Literal Representation], the above
WSDL definitions are mapped to the following service endpoint interface.

[#50634753_pgfId-1090727]## _// Java_

[#50634753_pgfId-1090728]##public interface ExampleSoap extends
java.rmi.Remote \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1090729]## String doExample(String field1, String
field2)

[#50634753_pgfId-1090730]## throws java.rmi.RemoteException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1090731]## DoExampleResponse
doAnotherExample(SOAPElement doAnotherExample)

[#50634753_pgfId-1090732]## throws java.rmi.RemoteException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1090733]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1090735]##This example assumes that the return type is
mapped to a _String_ for both methods. Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_88615[See WSDL Operation] for more details on
how WSDL operations are mapped.

[#50634753_pgfId-1090739]##In the above example mapping, the _part_
(named _body_ ) in the _message_ named _DoExample_ is mapped as a
wrapper. The elements field1 and field2 are mapped as separate
parameters with the corresponding Java types based on the standard XML
to Java type mapping.

[#50634753_pgfId-1101984]##Another possible mapping of the _doExample_
method is as follows. In this example, the _part_ named _body_ in the
_DoExample_ _message_ is mapped as an _xsd:complexType_ :

[#50634753_pgfId-1101987]## DoExampleResponse doExample(DoExample body)

[#50634753_pgfId-1102355]## throws java.rmi.RemoteException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1090740]##The JAX-RPC specification does not specify a
standard Java mapping for a _xsd:complexType_ with the
_xsd:anyAttribute_ . So the message part in the _DoAnotherExample_
message is mapped as a _SOAPElement_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1090741]##The following code snippet shows the client
code for invoking the _doAnotherExample_ method:

[#50634753_pgfId-1090742]##ExampleSoap ib = // ... get the Stub instance

[#50634753_pgfId-1090743]##SOAPFactory sef = SOAPFactory.newInstance();

[#50634753_pgfId-1090744]##SOAPElement request = sef.createElement(...);

[#50634753_pgfId-1090745]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1090746]##// populate the SOAPElement with attributes
and child elements

[#50634753_pgfId-1090748]##// ...

[#50634753_pgfId-1106621]##String response =
ib.doAnotherExample(request);

==== [#50634753_pgfId-1090750]##

image:jaxrpc-5.gif[image]

[#50634753_50628]##SOAP Fault

[#50634753_pgfId-1090751]##This section specifies the Java mapping of
the SOAP faults.

[#50634753_pgfId-1101169]##The _soap:fault_ element in the WSDL
specifies the contents of the _detail_ element of a SOAP fault. The
_name_ attribute relates the _soap:fault_ element to the _wsdl:fault_
element. The _wsdl:fault_ element (an optional element in a
_wsdl:operation_ ) specifies the abstract message format for any error
messages that may be output as a result of a remote operation.

[#50634753_pgfId-1090753]##The _soap:fault_ element is patterned after
the _soap:body_ element in terms of the literal or encoded use.
According to the WSDL 1.1 specification, the _soap:fault_ element must
contain only a single message part.

[#50634753_pgfId-1103177]##A SOAP fault is mapped to either a
_javax.xml.rpc.soap.SOAPFaultException_ , a service specific exception
class or _RemoteException_ .

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1090755]##SOAPFaultException

[#50634753_pgfId-1101129]##The _SOAPFaultException_ exception represents
a SOAP fault. This exception is thrown from the Java method mapped from
the corresponding _wsdl:operation_ . Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_88615[See WSDL Operation] for the mapping of
WSDL operations.

[#50634753_pgfId-1101133]##The message part in the SOAP fault maps to
the contents of _detail_ element accessible through the _getDetail_
method on the _SOAPFaultException_ . The method _createDetail_ on the
_javax.xml.soap.SOAPFactory_ creates an instance of the
_javax.xml.soap.Detail_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1106700]##The _faultstring_ provides a human-readable
description of the SOAP fault. The _faultcode_ element provides an
algorithmic mapping of the SOAP fault.

[#50634753_pgfId-1101134]##The following code snippet shows the
_SOAPFaultException_ :

[#50634753_pgfId-1101135]##package javax.xml.rpc.soap;

[#50634753_pgfId-1101136]##public class SOAPFaultException extends
java.lang.RuntimeException \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1101137]## public SOAPFaultException(QName faultcode,

[#50634753_pgfId-1101138]## String faultstring,

[#50634753_pgfId-1101139]## String faultactor,

[#50634753_pgfId-1101140]## javax.xml.soap.Detail detail) \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1101141]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1101142]## public QName getFaultCode() \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1101143]## public String getFaultString() \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1101144]## public String getFaultActor() \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1101145]## public javax.xml.soap.Detail getDetail() \{
... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1101146]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1110130]## 

==== [#50634753_pgfId-1110134]##

image:jaxrpc-5.gif[image]

[#50634753_33689]##SOAP Headerfault

[#50634753_pgfId-1110135]##The _soap:headerfault_ element is used to
specify SOAP header faults, that is, faults pertaining to the processing
of header elements in the message. According to the SOAP specification,
such faults must be carried within the Header element of the SOAP
envelope instead of the Body.

[#50634753_pgfId-1110151]##Unlike _soap:fault_ , which refers to a
_wsdl:fault_ , headerfaults refer directly to a message part. The
JAX-RPC specification only requires support for header faults with
literal use and referring (through their message part) to an
_xsd:element_ . When the header fault is transmitted, this element will
appear within the _SOAP-ENV:Header_ element (and not inside the detail
element of a _SOAP-ENV:Fault_ ), while the _SOAP-ENV:Body_ will contain
a _SOAP-ENV:Fault_ element whose _detail_ is either empty or
unspecified.

[#50634753_pgfId-1110175]##Aside from their different serialization,
SOAP headerfaults may be mapped to Java exceptions in the same way that
regular faults are, with the caveat that the mapping applies only when
the corresponding _soap:header_ has been mapped to a method argument
according to the explicit service context rules (see
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_49533[See Explicit Service Context]).

== [#50634753_pgfId-1004836]##

image:jaxrpc-3.gif[image]

[#50634753_38751]##SOAP Message With Attachments

image:jaxrpc-4.gif[image]

[#50634753_pgfId-1065731]##The JAX-RPC specification supports the use of
MIME encoded content in a remote method call to a target service
endpoint. This chapter specifies details on the following related
aspects:

[#50634753_pgfId-1047060]##SOAP Message with Attachments

[#50634753_pgfId-1047069]##WSDL 1.1 MIME Binding

[#50634753_pgfId-1058866]##Mapping between MIME types and Java types

==== [#50634753_pgfId-1047001]##

image:jaxrpc-5.gif[image]

SOAP Message with Attachments

[#50634753_pgfId-1046936]##A JAX-RPC runtime system implementation must
use the SOAP message with attachments link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_28069[See
W3 Note: SOAP Messages with Attachments:
http://www.w3.org/TR/SOAP-attachments] protocol to support MIME encoded
parameters or return value in a remote method call.

[#50634753_pgfId-1047717]##A SOAP message package with attachments is
constructed using the MIME _multipart/related_ type. The primary SOAP
1.1 message is carried in the root body part of the _multipart/related_
structure. The primary SOAP 1.1 message may reference additional
entities (termed as attachment or MIME parts) in the message package.

[#50634753_pgfId-1046951]##Both the header entries and body of the
primary SOAP 1.1 message refer to the MIME parts in the message package
using the _href_ attributes. A referenced MIME part contains either a
_Content-ID_ or _Content-Location_ MIME header. The SOAP messages with
Attachment specification link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_28069[See W3 Note:
SOAP Messages with Attachments: http://www.w3.org/TR/SOAP-attachments]
specifies more details on the resolution of URI references.

==== [#50634753_pgfId-1046787]##

image:jaxrpc-5.gif[image]

Java Types

[#50634753_pgfId-1047197]##A remote method in a Java service endpoint
interface may use the following Java types to represent MIME encoded
content:

[#50634753_pgfId-1047236]##Java classes based on the standard Java
mapping of MIME types. Refer to the section
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_49417[See Mapping between MIME types and Java
types] for more details.

[#50634753_pgfId-1047209]##Java class _javax.activation.DataHandler_ for
content with any MIME type

[#50634753_pgfId-1047361]##The JAX-RPC specification uses the JavaBeans
Activation Framework link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_86233[See JavaBeans
Activation Framework:
http://java.sun.com/products/javabeans/glasgow/jaf.html] to support
various MIME content types. The _DataHandler_ class provides a
consistent interface to the data represented in various MIME types. A
_DataHandler_ can be instantiated with data and a specific MIME type
using the constructor _DataHandler_ ( _Object_ _obj_ , _String_
_mime_type_ ).

[#50634753_pgfId-1047446]##The data represented by a _DataHandler_ may
be retrieved as a Java object or an _InputStream_ . The method
_DataHandler_ . _getContentType_ returns the MIME type of the
encapsulated data. The _DataHandler.getContent_ method returns a Java
object based on the MIME type of the encapsulated data.

[#50634753_pgfId-1047521]##A _DataHandler_ class uses the
_DataContentHandler_ interface to convert between a stream and specific
Java object based on the MIME type.

==== [#50634753_pgfId-1047647]##

image:jaxrpc-5.gif[image]

MIME Types

[#50634753_pgfId-1047648]##The JAX-RPC specification does not define any
restrictions on the MIME types. For example, the content in an
attachment (for a SOAP message with attachments) may be text, binary
image or a complex XML document.

[#50634753_pgfId-1103570]##The JAX-RPC runtime system determines the
MIME type of a MIME part carried in the SOAP message package by using
the following:

[#50634753_pgfId-1047668]##The MIME type defined in the _mime:content_
element for this MIME part in the WSDL MIME binding

[#50634753_pgfId-1047674]##The _Content-Type_ of the MIME part in the
SOAP message package

[#50634753_pgfId-1103787]##The MIME type of an attachment part in the
SOAP message is required to conform to the MIME type in the MIME binding
for an operation.

==== [#50634753_pgfId-1047645]##

image:jaxrpc-5.gif[image]

[#50634753_29571]##WSDL Requirements

[#50634753_pgfId-1104856]##A JAX-RPC implementation is required to
support mapping between Java and WSDL/XML for remote method calls with
the MIME encoded content.

[#50634753_pgfId-1047442]##A JAX-RPC implementation may use the MIME
binding (as specified in the WSDL 1.1 specification
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_91453[See Web Services Description Language
(WSDL) 1.1: http://www.w3.org/TR/wsdl]) to support remote method calls
with the MIME encoded content. In the mapped WSDL, MIME elements appear
under _wsdl:input_ and _wsdl:output_ elements in the _wsdl:binding_ .
The _mime_ : _multipartRelated_ element aggregates a set of MIME parts
(or attachment parts) into one message of MIME type "
_multipart/related_ ". The _mime:part_ element describes each attachment
part of such _multipart/related_ message.

[#50634753_pgfId-1103729]##The _mime:content_ elements appear within
each _mime:part_ to specify the concrete MIME type for this part. If
more than one _mime:content_ element appears inside a _mime:part_ ,
these are considered alternatives.

[#50634753_pgfId-1103676]##The _type_ attribute of the _mime:content_
element specifies the MIME type for an attachment part. The _part_
attribute is used to specify the name of the message part. The _type_
attribute may use _*_ wild cards to specify a set of acceptable MIME
types. An example is _image/*_ for all image types.

[#50634753_pgfId-1103630]##The _parts_ attribute in the _wsdl:input_ and
_wsdl:output_ elements (defined per _operation_ in the _wsdl:binding_ )
lists parts that appear in the SOAP body portion of the message. The
unlisted parts of a message appear in the attachment parts of the SOAP
message in the case of the _multipart/related_ MIME binding.

==== [#50634753_pgfId-1047196]##

image:jaxrpc-5.gif[image]

[#50634753_49417]##Mapping between MIME types and Java types

[#50634753_pgfId-1067918]##The following table specifies the standard
Java mapping for a subset of the MIME types.

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1067891]##[#50634753_60001]##Mapping of MIME Types

[#50634753_pgfId-1067895]##MIME Type

[#50634753_pgfId-1067897]##Java Type

[#50634753_pgfId-1067899]## _image/gif_

[#50634753_pgfId-1067901]## _java.awt.Image_

[#50634753_pgfId-1067903]## _image/jpeg_

[#50634753_pgfId-1067905]## _java.awt.Image_

[#50634753_pgfId-1067907]## _text/plain_

[#50634753_pgfId-1067909]## _java.lang.String_

[#50634753_pgfId-1067911]## _multipart/*_

[#50634753_pgfId-1067913]## _javax.mail.internet.MimeMultipart_

[#50634753_pgfId-1094220]##text/xml or application/xml

[#50634753_pgfId-1094218]##javax.xml.transform.Source

[#50634753_pgfId-1094452]##The Java to WSDL/XML and WSDL/XML to Java
mapping for the MIME types is required to conform to the above mapping.
This mapping is reflected in the mapped Java method signatures and WSDL
description. A WSDL/XML to Java mapping tool is required to provide an
option to map the above set of MIME types to the
_javax.activation.DataHandler_ class. The _DataHandler_ class provides
methods to get access to the stream representation of the data for a
MIME type.

[#50634753_pgfId-1103950]##A Java to WSDL mapping tool is required to
provide a facility for specifying metadata related to the above mapping
between Java and MIME types. This metadata identifies whether a Java
type is mapped to a MIME type (using the WSDL MIME binding) or is mapped
to an XML schema type (based on the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_19087[See
XML to Java Type Mapping]). For example, a _java.lang.String_ can be
mapped to either an _xsd:string_ or MIME type _text/plain_ . The mapping
metadata identifies a specific mapping.

[#50634753_pgfId-1094461]##If a MIME type is mapped to the
_javax.activation.DataHandler_ , the _getContent_ method of the
_DataHandler_ class must return instance of the corresponding Java type
for a specific MIME content type.

[#50634753_pgfId-1094453]##A JAX-RPC implementation is required to
support the above MIME types (as specified in the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_60001[See Mapping of MIME Types]) and provide
implementation of the required _javax.activation.DataContentHandler_
classes.

[#50634753_pgfId-1109507]##Due to limitations in the platform, a JAX-RPC
implementation is required only to support decoding images of type
_image/gif_ , but not encoding of the same.

[#50634753_pgfId-1047853]##A JAX-RPC implementation is not required to
support MIME types beyond that specified in the above table. These
additional MIME types may be mapped and supported using the
_javax.activation.DataHandler_ class and Java Activation Framework.

== [#50634753_pgfId-1046102]##

image:jaxrpc-3.gif[image]

[#50634753_60605]##JAX-RPC Core APIs

image:jaxrpc-4.gif[image]

[#50634753_pgfId-1055644]##This chapter specifies JAX-RPC APIs that
support the JAX-RPC runtime mechanisms. These APIs are packaged in the
_javax.xml.rpc_ package. The link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_73719[See SOAP
Message Handlers] specifies the SOAP message handler APIs.

==== [#50634753_pgfId-1055649]##

image:jaxrpc-5.gif[image]

Server side APIs

[#50634753_pgfId-1067977]##It is important to note that the JAX-RPC
specification does not define and require any standard APIs for the EJB
container based implementation of a JAX-RPC server-side runtime system.
Refer to the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_20289[See Service Endpoint Model]
for API specified for the servlet endpoint model.

[#50634753_pgfId-1064806]##The internals of a J2EE container based
JAX-RPC runtime system are implementation specific.

==== [#50634753_pgfId-1006851]##

image:jaxrpc-5.gif[image]

[#50634753_55054]##Client side APIs

[#50634753_pgfId-1055656]##The JAX-RPC specifies the following client
side APIs:

[#50634753_pgfId-1055657]##The _javax.xml.rpc.Stub_ interface

[#50634753_pgfId-1055671]##The _javax.xml.rpc.Call_ interface for the
dynamic invocation of a JAX-RPC service

[#50634753_pgfId-1055659]##The _javax.xml.rpc.Service_ interface

[#50634753_pgfId-1092047]##The _javax.xml.rpc.ServiceFactory_ class

[#50634753_pgfId-1067980]##The _javax.xml.rpc.JAXRPCException_ class

[#50634753_pgfId-1055679]##A JAX-RPC runtime system implementation is
required to implement the above APIs.

[#50634753_pgfId-1088091]##The link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_40687[See
Service Client Programming Model] describes the programming model for
the use of these APIs by a service client.

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1055687]##[#50634753_34332]##Generated Stub Class

[#50634753_pgfId-1072473]##A WSDL to Java mapping tool generates a stub
class during the import of a service described in a WSDL document. The
JAX-RPC specification does not require that a stub class be generated
only through the mapping of a WSDL document. For example, a stub class
may be generated using a service endpoint interface and additional
information about the protocol binding.

[#50634753_pgfId-1072400]##All generated stub classes are required to
implement the _javax.xml.rpc.Stub_ interface. An instance of a stub
class represents a client side proxy or stub instance for the target
service endpoint.

[#50634753_pgfId-1072428]##The following code snippet shows the
_javax.xml.rpc.Stub_ interface:

[#50634753_pgfId-1072429]##package javax.xml.rpc;

[#50634753_pgfId-1072430]##public interface Stub \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1064534]## // ... Methods specified later

[#50634753_pgfId-1090914]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1072457]##A generated stub class is required to
implement a service endpoint interface. The name of a generated stub
class is either _<BindingName>_Stub_ or is implementation specific. In
the former case, the name of the generated stub class is derived from
the _name_ attribute of the corresponding _wsdl:binding_ element in the
imported WSDL service description. The _wsdl:binding_ element binds an
abstract _wsdl:portType_ to a specific protocol and transport.

[#50634753_pgfId-1088100]##Note that the JAX-RPC specification does not
require that a generated stub class be binding and transport neutral. A
stub class should be bound to a specific protocol and transport.

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1006559]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1033344]##The following diagram shows an illustrative
example of the stub class hierarchy. The diagram shows the generated
StockServiceSoapBinding __Stub_ class that implements the
_javax.xml.rpc.Stub_ and _com.example.StockQuoteProvider_ interfaces
where the _StockQuoteProvider_ interface is the service endpoint
interface.

[#50634753_pgfId-1006770]##The diagram also shows the generated stub
class using the standard _javax.xml.rpc_ package and a vendor specific
JAX-RPC implementation package. For example, a generated stub class may
be based on either the standard APIs that are specified in the
_javax.xml.rpc_ package or vendor specific JAX-RPC implementation APIs.

image:jaxrpc-18.gif[image]

[#50634753_pgfId-1091084]##The following code snippet shows how a J2SE
based service client uses a stub instance. This example uses a generated
stub class:

[#50634753_pgfId-1091085]## com.example.StockQuoteProvider_Stub sqp = //
get the Stub instance

[#50634753_pgfId-1091087]## float quote = sqp.getLastTradePrice("ACME");

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1057618]##[#50634753_21802]##Stub Configuration

[#50634753_pgfId-1091113]##A stub instance must be configured such that
a service client can use this stub instance to invoke a remote method on
the target service endpoint. A stub instance may be configured in one of
the following manners:

[#50634753_pgfId-1091114]##Static configuration based on the WSDL
description of a target service endpoint. Examples of such configuration
include protocol binding specified using the _wsdl:binding_ and
_soap:binding_ elements; target service endpoint address specified using
the _wsdl:port_ element.

[#50634753_pgfId-1091115]##Dynamic runtime configuration using the
_javax.xml.rpc.Stub_ API. This section specifies further details of this
type of configuration.

[#50634753_pgfId-1091116]##The JAX-RPC specification does not require
support for protocol and transport neutral stub classes that are
dynamically configurable for different protocols and transports. A stub
class should be bound to a specific protocol and transport.

[#50634753_pgfId-1091117]##The _javax.xml.rpc.Stub_ interface provides
an extensible property mechanism for the dynamic configuration of a stub
instance. The following code snippet shows the _Stub_ interface:

[#50634753_pgfId-1091118]##package javax.xml.rpc;

[#50634753_pgfId-1091119]##public interface Stub \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1098390]## // ...

[#50634753_pgfId-1091120]## void _setProperty(String name, Object
value);

[#50634753_pgfId-1091121]## Object _getProperty(String name);

[#50634753_pgfId-1091122]## java.util.Iterator _getPropertyNames();

[#50634753_pgfId-1091123]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1091580]##The __setProperty_ method sets the value of a
property configured on the stub instance. This method throws the
_javax.xml.rpc.JAXRPCException_ in the following cases:

[#50634753_pgfId-1098682]##If an optional standard property name is
specified, however this _Stub_ implementation class does not support the
configuration of this property.

[#50634753_pgfId-1098688]##If an invalid or unsupported property name is
specified or if a value of mismatched property type is passed. An
example is an illegal property with the standard property name prefix
_javax.xml.rpc_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1098703]##If there is any error in the configuration of
a valid property.

[#50634753_pgfId-1099452]##Note that the __setProperty_ method may not
check validity of a configured property value. An example is the
standard property for the target service endpoint address that is not
checked for validity in the __setProperty_ method. In this case, any
stub configuration errors are detected at the remote method invocation.

[#50634753_pgfId-1091125]##The __getProperty_ method gets the value of a
property configured on the stub instance. This method should throw the
_javax.xml.rpc.JAXRPCException_ if an invalid or unsupported property
name is passed.

[#50634753_pgfId-1091126]##The __getPropertyNames_ returns the names of
the supported configurable properties for this stub class.

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1091127]##Standard Properties

[#50634753_pgfId-1091128]##The JAX-RPC specification specifies a
standard set of properties that are protocol and transport independent.
These standard properties may be passed to the __getProperty_ and
__setProperty_ methods.

[#50634753_pgfId-1091129]##A stub class is not required to support these
standard properties. The names and types of these properties are as
follows. This table also specifies whether or not a _Stub_
implementation is required to support a specific standard property:

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1091132]##Standard Properties for Stub Configuration

[#50634753_pgfId-1091138]##Name of Property

[#50634753_pgfId-1091140]##Type of Property

[#50634753_pgfId-1091142]##Description and Required/Optional support

[#50634753_pgfId-1091144]## _javax.xml.rpc._

[#50634753_pgfId-1097891]## _security.auth._

[#50634753_pgfId-1097894]## _username_

[#50634753_pgfId-1091147]## _java.lang._

[#50634753_pgfId-1091930]## _String_

[#50634753_pgfId-1091149]##User name for authentication

[#50634753_pgfId-1098651]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1098652]##Required to support HTTP Basic
Authentication. Refer to the link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_33108[See HTTP
Basic Authentication] for more details.

[#50634753_pgfId-1098653]##
