===== [#50634753_pgfId-1056770]##[#50634753_72254]##Dynamic Proxy

[#50634753_pgfId-1039299]##The JAX-RPC specification requires support
for the dynamic proxy for invoking a service endpoint. A dynamic proxy
class supports a service endpoint interface dynamically at runtime
without requiring any code generation of a stub class that implements a
specific service endpoint interface.

[#50634753_pgfId-1039295]##Refer to the J2SE
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_70636[See J2SE: http://java.sun.com/j2se/]
documentation for more details on the dynamic proxy APIs
_java.lang.reflect.Proxy_ and _java.lang.reflect.InvocationHandler_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1034346]##The _getPort_ method on the
_javax.xml.rpc.Service_ interface provide support for the creation of a
dynamic proxy. The serviceEndpointInterface parameter specifies the
service endpoint interface that is supported by the created dynamic
proxy. The service endpoint interface must conform to the JAX-RPC
specification.:

[#50634753_pgfId-1068162]##package javax.xml.rpc;

[#50634753_pgfId-1068163]##public interface Service \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1068165]## java.rmi.Remote getPort(QName portName,

[#50634753_pgfId-1068166]## Class serviceEndpointInterface)

[#50634753_pgfId-1068167]## throws ServiceException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1033755]## // ...

[#50634753_pgfId-1065216]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1103391]##This method throws _ServiceException_ if
there is an error in creation of the dynamic proxy or if there is any
missing WSDL related metadata that is required. The JAX-RPC
specification does not require that the _getPort_ method fully validate
the passed serviceEndpointInterface against the corresponding WSDL
definitions. A JAX-RPC implementation may choose to perform either lazy
or eager validation in an implementation specific manner.

[#50634753_pgfId-1098648]##A dynamic proxy is required to also support
the _javax.xml.rpc.Stub_ interface. This provides support for the
configuration of a dynamic proxy. Refer to the
link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_21802[See Stub Configuration] for additional
details.

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1063916]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1063917]##The following example shows the use of a
dynamic proxy for invoking an operation on the target service endpoint.
Note that this example does not use any generated stub class that
implements the StockQuoteProvider service endpoint interface:

[#50634753_pgfId-1063918]## javax.xml.rpc.Service service = //... access
a Service instance

[#50634753_pgfId-1063919]## com.example.StockQuoteProvider sqp =

[#50634753_pgfId-1063920]##
(com.example.StockQuoteProvider)service.getPort(

[#50634753_pgfId-1063921]## portName, StockQuoteProvider.class);

[#50634753_pgfId-1063922]## float price = sqp.getLastTradePrice("ACME");

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1055750]##[#50634753_87541]##DII Call Interface

[#50634753_pgfId-1056414]##The _javax.xml.rpc.Call_ interface provides
support for the dynamic invocation of an operation on the target service
endpoint. The _javax.xml.rpc.Service_ interface acts as a factory for
the creation of _Call_ instances.

[#50634753_pgfId-1065224]##A client side JAX-RPC runtime system
implementation is required to implement the _Call_ interface.

[#50634753_pgfId-1068181]##The _createCall_ method on the _Service_
interface may create a _Call_ object with an internal implementation
specific in-memory model of the WSDL description of the service. The
_portName_ in the _createCall_ method identifies the target service
endpoint.

[#50634753_pgfId-1068182]##The _createCall_ method with no parameters
creates an empty _Call_ object that needs to be configured using the
setter methods on the _Call_ interface.

[#50634753_pgfId-1056430]##The following code snippet shows the
_Service_ and _Call_ interfaces. Refer to the Javadocs for a complete
API specification:

[#50634753_pgfId-1068171]##package javax.xml.rpc;

[#50634753_pgfId-1068172]##public interface Service \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1068173]## Call createCall() throws ServiceException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1068174]## Call createCall(QName portName) throws
ServiceException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1068175]## Call createCall(QName portName, String
operationName)

[#50634753_pgfId-1068176]## throws ServiceException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1080588]## Call createCall(QName portName, QName
operationName)

[#50634753_pgfId-1080589]## throws ServiceException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1103428]## Call[] getCalls(QName portName) throws
ServiceException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1068177]## // ... Other methods not shown here

[#50634753_pgfId-1055760]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1090086]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1090092]##// Typesafe Enumeration for ParameterMode

[#50634753_pgfId-1091507]##public class ParameterMode \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1091508]## private final String mode;

[#50634753_pgfId-1091511]## private ParameterMode(String mode) \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1091512]## this.mode = mode;

[#50634753_pgfId-1091513]## }

[#50634753_pgfId-1091515]## public String toString() \{ return mode; }

[#50634753_pgfId-1091517]## public static final ParameterMode IN = new
ParameterMode("IN");

[#50634753_pgfId-1091519]## public static final ParameterMode OUT = new
ParameterMode("OUT");

[#50634753_pgfId-1091521]## public static final ParameterMode INOUT =

[#50634753_pgfId-1099357]## new ParameterMode("INOUT");

[#50634753_pgfId-1091524]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1074580]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1074581]## // Remote Method Invocation methods

[#50634753_pgfId-1074582]## Object invoke(QName operationName, Object[]
inputParams)

[#50634753_pgfId-1080532]## throws java.rmi.RemoteException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1080529]## Object invoke(Object[] inputParams)

[#50634753_pgfId-1094274]## throws java.rmi.RemoteException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1074583]## void invokeOneWay(Object[] inputParams);

[#50634753_pgfId-1086507]## 

[#50634753_pgfId-1080542]## java.util.Map getOutputParams();

[#50634753_pgfId-1103930]## java.util.List getOutputValues();

[#50634753_pgfId-1103919]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1055795]##Once a _Call_ instance is created, various
setter and getter methods are used to configure this _Call_ instance.
The configuration of a _Call_ instance includes the following:

[#50634753_pgfId-1055796]##Name of a specific operation

[#50634753_pgfId-1087256]##Port type for the target service endpoint

[#50634753_pgfId-1073261]##Address of the target service endpoint

[#50634753_pgfId-1055799]##Properties specific to the binding to a
protocol and transport: example, SOAPAction URI for the SOAP binding to
HTTP. The standard properties are specified later in this section.

[#50634753_pgfId-1055800]##Name, type and mode ( _IN_ , _INOUT_ , _OUT_
) of the parameters. These properties are optional.

[#50634753_pgfId-1074433]##Return type

[#50634753_pgfId-1101068]##A setter method should throw
_javax.xml.rpc.JAXRPCException_ in the following cases:

[#50634753_pgfId-1101055]##If an optional standard property name is
specified, however this _Call_ implementation class does not support the
configuration of this property.

[#50634753_pgfId-1101056]##If an invalid or unsupported property name is
specified or if a value of mismatched property type is passed. An
example is an illegal property name with the standard property name
prefix _javax.xml.rpc_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1101057]##If there is any error in the configuration of
a valid property.

[#50634753_pgfId-1101058]##Note that a setter method may not check
validity of a configured property value. An example is the standard
property for the target service endpoint address that is not checked for
validity. In this case, any configuration errors are detected at the
invoke time.

[#50634753_pgfId-1080561]##In terms of the specification of parameters
and return value, a _Call_ implementation class is required to support
the following cases:

[#50634753_pgfId-1068186]##The _Call_ implementation class determines
the types of the parameters and return value from the invocation of
_addParameter_ and _setReturnType_ methods in the client code. The
method _isParameterAndReturnSpecRequired_ is required to return _true_
in this case.

[#50634753_pgfId-1056475]##The _Call_ implementation class determines
the types and modes of the parameters in an implementation specific
manner. For example, a _Call_ implementation class may determine
parameter types by using Java reflection on parameters, using WSDL
service description and the configured type mapping registry. In this
case, the client code is not required to invoke any _addParameter_ and
_setReturnType_ methods before calling the _invoke_ method. The method
_isParameterAndReturnSpec-Required_ is required to return _false_ in
this case. The methods _addParameter_ , _removeAllParameters_ and
_setReturnType_ may throw _JAXRPCException_ if invoked in this case.

====== [#50634753_pgfId-1056464]##Invocation Modes

[#50634753_pgfId-1056515]##The _Call_ implementation class is required
to support the following invocation modes:

[#50634753_pgfId-1057576]##Synchronous request-response mode: The
_invoke_ method calls a specified operation using a synchronous
request-response interaction mode. The _invoke_ method takes as
parameters the object values corresponding to the parameter types. The
implementation of the _invoke_ method checks whether the passed
parameter values match the number, order and types of parameters
specified in the corresponding WSDL specification of the same operation.
The _invoke_ method is required to throw exception _java.rmi_ .
_RemoteException_ if there is any error in the remote method invocation.
The method throws _JAXRPCException_ if the _Call_ object is not
configured properly or if parameters and return type are incorrectly
specified.

[#50634753_pgfId-1057583]##One-way mode: The _invokeOneWay_ method
invokes a remote method using the one-way interaction mode. The client
thread does not block waiting for the completion of the processing of
this remote method invocation on the service endpoint. When the protocol
in use is SOAP/HTTP, the client should block until an HTTP response code
has been received or an error occurs. Reception of a response code
simply means that the transmission of the request is complete, and not
that the request was accepted or processed. This method must not throw
any remote exceptions. This method is required to throw a
_JAXRPCException_ if there is an error in the configuration of the
_Call_ object (example: a non-void return type has been incorrectly
specified for the one-way call) or if there is any error during the
invocation of the one-way remote call.

[#50634753_pgfId-1080568]##The method _getOutputParams_ returns a
_java.util.Map_ of \{name, value} for the output parameters for the last
invoked operation. The parameter names in the returned _Map_ are of the
type _java.lang.String_ . The type of a value depends on the mapping
between the Java and XML types. This method is required to throw
_JAXRPCException_ if invoked for a one-way operation or if invoked
before any _invoke_ method has been called.

[#50634753_pgfId-1103920]##The method _getOutputValues_ returns a list
(of Java type _java.util.List_ ) of values for the output parameters.
This method is required to throw _JAXRPCException_ if invoked for a
one-way operation or if invoked before any _invoke_ method has been
called.

====== [#50634753_pgfId-1063929]##Standard Properties

[#50634753_pgfId-1073494]##The JAX-RPC specification specifies a
standard set of properties that may be passed to the _Call_ .
_setProperty_ method. A _Call_ implementation class may also support
additional set of properties. However, the specification of these
additional properties is out of scope for JAX-RPC.

[#50634753_pgfId-1073490]##The names and types of these properties are
as follows. The following table also specifies whether or not a _Call_
implementation is required to support a specific standard property:

====== [#50634753_pgfId-1090174]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1068009]##The following code example shows a typical
use of the _Call_ interface:

[#50634753_pgfId-1087312]## _javax.xml.rpc.Service service = //... get a
Service instance_

[#50634753_pgfId-1087313]## _javax.xml.rpc.Call_ call =
service.createCall(

[#50634753_pgfId-1087314]## portName, “<operationName>”);

[#50634753_pgfId-1087315]## call.addParameter(“param1”, <xsd:string>,

[#50634753_pgfId-1090164]## ParameterMode.IN);

[#50634753_pgfId-1087316]## call.addParameter(“param2”, <xsd:string>,

[#50634753_pgfId-1090166]## ParameterMode.OUT);

[#50634753_pgfId-1087317]## call.setReturnType(<xsd:int>);

[#50634753_pgfId-1087318]## Object[] inParams = new Object[]
\{“<SomeString>”};

[#50634753_pgfId-1087319]## Integer ret = (Integer)
call.invoke(inParams);

[#50634753_pgfId-1087320]## Map outParams = call.getOutputParams();

[#50634753_pgfId-1087321]## String outValue =
(String)outParams.get(“param2”);

[#50634753_pgfId-1068017]##An alternative way to invoke the same remote
method using the DII _Call_ interface is as follows. In this case, the
_Call_ implementation class takes the responsibility of determining the
corresponding types for the parameters and return value:

[#50634753_pgfId-1068018]## _javax.xml.rpc.Service service = //... get a
Service instance_

[#50634753_pgfId-1068019]## _javax.xml.rpc.Call_ call =
service.createCall(

[#50634753_pgfId-1068020]## portName, “<operationName>”);

[#50634753_pgfId-1068021]## Object[] params = new Object[]
\{“<SomeString>”};

[#50634753_pgfId-1087338]## Integer ret = (Integer) call.invoke(params);

[#50634753_pgfId-1092761]## String outValue =
(String)call.getOutputParams().get(“param2”);

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1092050]##Abstract ServiceFactory[#50634753_30216]##

[#50634753_pgfId-1092051]##The _javax.xml.rpc.ServiceFactory_ is an
abstract class that provides a factory for the creation of instances of
the type _javax.xml.rpc.Service_ . This abstract class follows the
abstract static factory design pattern. This enables a J2SE based client
to create a _Service_ instance in a portable manner without using the
constructor of the _Service_ implementation class.

[#50634753_pgfId-1092052]##package javax.xml.rpc;

[#50634753_pgfId-1092053]##public abstract class ServiceFactory \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1092054]## protected ServiceFactory() \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1092055]## public static ServiceFactory newInstance()

[#50634753_pgfId-1092056]## throws ServiceException \{ ...}

[#50634753_pgfId-1092059]## public abstract Service createService(

[#50634753_pgfId-1092060]## java.net.URL wsdlDocumentLocation,

[#50634753_pgfId-1092061]## QName serviceName)

[#50634753_pgfId-1093334]## throws ServiceException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1093335]## public abstract Service createService(

[#50634753_pgfId-1093336]## QName serviceName)

[#50634753_pgfId-1093337]## throws ServiceException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1116568]## public abstract Service loadService(Class
serviceInterface)

[#50634753_pgfId-1116569]## throws ServiceException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1111083]## public abstract Service loadService(

[#50634753_pgfId-1111084]## java.net.URL wsdlDocumentLocation,

[#50634753_pgfId-1111085]## Class serviceInterface,

[#50634753_pgfId-1111086]## java.util.Properties properties)

[#50634753_pgfId-1111087]## throws ServiceException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1111088]## public abstract Service loadService(

[#50634753_pgfId-1111089]## java.net.URL wsdlDocumentLocation,

[#50634753_pgfId-1111090]## QName serviceName,

[#50634753_pgfId-1111091]## java.util.Properties properties)

[#50634753_pgfId-1111092]## throws ServiceException;

[#50634753_pgfId-1093338]##}

[#50634753_pgfId-1093339]##A client-side JAX-RPC runtime system is
required to provide implementation of the abstract _ServiceFactory_
class. The _ServiceFactory_ implementation class is set using the system
property named _SERVICEFACTORY_PROPERTY_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1116578]##A JAX-RPC implementation that does not use a
consistent naming convention for generated service implementation
classes must allow an application developer to specify sufficient
configuration information so that the
_ServiceFactory.loadService(Class)_ method will succeed provided all the
generated artifacts are packaged with the application. Examples of
configuration information include: properties- or XML-based
configuration files that are looked up as resources using the
_java.lang.ClassLoader_ _getResource_ / _getResources_ APIs, system
properties and the preferences APIs (java.util.prefs) introduces in J2SE
1.4.

[#50634753_pgfId-1092068]##A J2SE service client should use this model
to get access to the _Service_ object. A J2SE based service client may
use the JNDI naming context to lookup a service instance.

[#50634753_pgfId-1116605]##A J2EE-based service client should not use
the _ServiceFactory_ APIs to access a service. Moreover, packaging
implementation-specific artifacts (including classes and configuration
information) with an application is strongly discouraged as it would
make the application non-portable. Instead, J2EE-based service clients
should use JNDI to lookup an instance of a _Service_ class as specified
in JSR-109 link:jaxrpc.htm#50634753_70338[See JSR 109: Implementing
Enterprise Web Services: http://jcp.org/jsr/detail?id=109].

======= [#50634753_pgfId-1092069]##Example

[#50634753_pgfId-1092070]##The following code snippet shows the use of
the _ServiceFactory_ .

[#50634753_pgfId-1092071]##Service service =
ServiceFactory.newInstance().createService(...);

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1071339]##ServiceException

[#50634753_pgfId-1099380]##[#50634753_69693]##The
_javax.xml.rpc.ServiceException_ is thrown from the methods defined in
the _javax.xml.rpc.Service_ and _javax.xml.rpc.ServiceFactory_ APIs. The
following code snippet shows the _ServiceException_ :

[#50634753_pgfId-1099385]##package javax.xml.rpc;

[#50634753_pgfId-1099386]##public class ServiceException extends
java.lang.Exception \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1099387]## public ServiceException() \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1099388]## public ServiceException(String message) \{
... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1099389]## public ServiceException(Throwable cause) \{
... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1099390]## public ServiceException(String message,
Throwable cause) \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1099391]## public Throwable getLinkedCause() \{ ... }

[#50634753_pgfId-1099392]##}

===== [#50634753_pgfId-1099379]##JAXRPCException

[#50634753_pgfId-1071346]##The _javax.xml.rpc.JAXRPCException_ is thrown
from the core APIs to indicate exceptions related to the JAX-RPC runtime
mechanisms. A _JAXRPCException_ is mapped to a
_java.rmi.RemoteException_ if the former is thrown during the processing
of a remote method invocation.

[#50634753_pgfId-1071347]##package javax.xml.rpc;

[#50634753_pgfId-1071348]##public class JAXRPCException extends
java.lang.RuntimeException \{

[#50634753_pgfId-1071349]## public JAXRPCException() \{ ... }

... }
